- status: completed

- step_id: 03-010
- step_title: implement-clean-quit-and-endoom-policy
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 clean-quit and ENDOOM policy as a self-contained audit ledger plus reference handler at `src/bootstrap/implement-clean-quit-and-endoom-policy.ts`. The audit module declares the canonical 5-step `I_Quit` sequence (`D_QuitNetGame → G_CheckDemoStatus → M_SaveDefaults → I_ShutdownGraphics → exit(0)`, all unconditional, exit code 0), the canonical 4-step `I_Error` cleanup sequence (`if (demorecording) G_CheckDemoStatus(); → D_QuitNetGame() → I_ShutdownGraphics() → exit(-1)`, with only the first cleanup gated on `demorecording`, exit code -1), the canonical 4-step `I_Error` stderr prologue (`fprintf("Error: ") → vfprintf(error,argptr) → fprintf("\n") → fflush(stderr)`), the verbatim source-literal fingerprints (stderr prefix `"Error: "`, trailing newline `"\n"`, ENDOOM lump name `"ENDOOM"`, lump size 4000 bytes, 80 columns × 25 rows, 2 bytes per cell), the structural absence of every Chocolate Doom 2.2.1-only quit-stage feature from linuxdoom-1.10 (eight items: `I_AtExit`, `lifoTraversal`, `runOnErrorFilter`, `D_Endoom`, `I_Endoom`, `S_Shutdown`, `I_ShutdownTimer`, `recursiveCallGuard`), and the explicit absence of `M_SaveDefaults` from the `I_Error` cleanup path (vanilla intentionally skips the config save on the error path because the defaults table may be in an inconsistent state when an error fires). The audit ledger pins thirty-one contract clauses (eight `I_Quit` clauses, twelve `I_Error` clauses, three linuxdoom-source-absence clauses, four ENDOOM-lump structural clauses, four Chocolate-only-omission clauses) and the derived-invariant ledger pins twenty-four invariants, witnessed by forty pinned probes that exercise every query kind (quit-op-at-index, error-cleanup-op-at-index, error-prologue-op-at-index, op-condition with quit/error-cleanup/error-prologue phase discriminators, op-presence-in-quit, op-presence-in-error-cleanup, quit-total-step-count, error-cleanup-op-count, quit-exit-code, error-exit-code, error-stderr-prefix, error-trailing-newline, endoom-lump-name, endoom-lump-size-bytes, endoom-grid-columns, endoom-grid-rows, endoom-bytes-per-cell, linuxdoom-has-feature, error-has-recursive-guard, quit-op-precedes-quit-op). Exposed reference handler `REFERENCE_VANILLA_CLEAN_QUIT_AND_ENDOOM_POLICY_HANDLER`, cross-checker `crossCheckVanillaCleanQuitAndEndoomPolicy`, and convenience derivation helper `deriveExpectedVanillaCleanQuitAndEndoomPolicyResult`. Authority order is per `plan_vanilla_parity/SOURCE_CATALOG.md` (DOS binary > IWAD > Windows oracle > linuxdoom-1.10 source > Chocolate Doom 2.2.1) but the cleanup contract is pinned against authority 4 (id Software `linuxdoom-1.10/i_system.c` `I_Quit()` and `I_Error()` are the verbatim source of the 5-step / 4-step cleanup sequences, the demorecording gate around `G_CheckDemoStatus` in `I_Error`, the `"Error: "` prefix and `"\n"` trailing newline literals, the `exit(0)` and `exit(-1)` exit codes, and the structural absence of `D_Endoom`/`I_Endoom`/`I_AtExit`); ENDOOM lump structural facts are pinned against authority 2 (the IWAD `DOOM1.WAD`) and cross-validated against the existing `src/ui/endoom.ts` parser constants without importing from that runtime file (the audit module deliberately avoids importing from any runtime quit/ENDOOM module so a corrupted runtime cannot silently calibrate the audit's own probe table). Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-clean-quit-and-endoom-policy.test.ts` (109 tests, 553 expects) covering ledger shape (31 contract clauses, 24 derived invariants, 40 probes — every id unique, every clause cites a real linuxdoom-1.10 source file or the IWAD, every IWAD clause is pinned against `DOOM1.WAD`, every Chocolate-omission clause names its specific Chocolate addition), the canonical 5-step `I_Quit` order (verbatim sequence, 0-based indices, four cleanup steps + one termination step, every cleanup step unconditional), the canonical 4-step `I_Error` cleanup order (only `G_CheckDemoStatus` gated on `demorecording`, `M_SaveDefaults` absent from the cleanup, three cleanup steps + one termination step), the canonical 4-step `I_Error` prologue order (every prologue step unconditional with `error-prologue` phase), the eight Chocolate-only quit-stage features absence list, top-level constants pin `I_Quit` exit code at 0, `I_Error` exit code at -1, stderr prefix `"Error: "` (length 7), trailing newline `"\n"` (length 1), ENDOOM lump name `"ENDOOM"`, lump size 4000 bytes, grid 80×25, bytes-per-cell 2, total cell count 2000 (cross-validates the byte-product invariant `cells × bytes-per-cell == lump size`), every probe declares an expected answer field consistent with its query kind, every witness invariant id refers to a declared derived `I_ShutdownTimer` included in the quit sequence, (e) `D_Endoom` reported as present in linuxdoom-1.10, (f) `I_AtExit` stack reported as present in linuxdoom-1.10, (g) recursive-call guard inside code (1 instead of -1), (l) different stderr prefix (lowercase "error: "), (m) wrong ENDOOM lump size (4096 instead of 4000), (n) wrong ENDOOM grid (40×25 CGA instead of 80×25 VGA), (o) `D_QuitNetGame` reported as following `I_ShutdownGraphics` in `I_Quit` (reversed precedence), (p) wrong ENDOOM lump name (`ENDOOM2`), (q) dropped trailing newline, (r) wrong cleanup op count (4 - open_risks: The audit module is a static ledger plus reference handler — it does NOT drive the runtime `bun run doom.ts` entry point. A future implementation step (or an oracle follow-up that observes `doom/DOOMD.EXE` directly) must wire the canonical 5-step `I_Quit` and 4-step `I_Error` skeletons into the runtime quit machinery. The current `src/bootstrap/quitFlow.ts` models the Chocolate-shaped `QuitFlow` (with `I_AtExit` registration stack, 8-handler LIFO traversal, and `runOnError` filter) and is NOT vanilla-1.9-faithful — it must be replaced or rewired by a downstream step before `bun run doom.ts` can claim parity with vanilla 1.9 quit/error behaviour. The DOS binary ENDOOM display semantics (when ENDOOM is read, how it's painted to the text-mode buffer at 0xB8000, whether DOS DOOM waits for keypress before exit) are NOT pinned by this audit because they are not visible in the linuxdoom-1.10 source we treat as authority 4 — a future oracle-capture step targeting `doom/DOOMD.EXE` under DOSBox should pin the exact ENDOOM display position relative to `I_ShutdownGraphics` and the keypress-wait semantics. The cross-checker is exact-equality on every probe field; future audits that extend the probe set must add new probes without mutating prior expectations (the audit ledger is intentionally append-only). The recurring parallel-lane working-tree race documented in prior 01-008 / 01-009 / 01-010 / 01-011 / 01-012 / 03-008 / 03-009 / 04-005 / 04-006 / 05-005 / 05-006 / 05-007 / 03-006 / 03-007 open_risks is still active: the fourteen `bun test` failures (3 WAD-asset inventory + 1 core-math inventory + 4 step-file-heading/plan-validation + 4 isolation probe + 2 cataloged-file failures) are caused by parallel-lane committed state, parallel-lane untracked state, and prior step-file heading flips that the prior inventory snapshots and validator pre-date. The mitigation pattern remains: (a) document the failures in `tests_run` as expected and outside this lane's write lock, (b) commit only this lane's own write-locked files plus plan-control updates, (c) await the inventory lane's snapshot regeneration and a future governance step un-flipping the 01-010/03-008/03-009/05-007 step-file headings. Lane lock `99274bec-21d6-47c6-9f44-30c71db90cb0` is held by the launcher and will be released on normal exit. No proprietary assets were modified or staged; `doom/`, `iwad/`, and `reference/` were strictly read-only.

## 2026-04-27 - 01-012 inventory-audio-modules

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: inventory
- lock_id: 49f80485-207a-47cf-8dbe-efa38bf6b262
- step_id: 01-012
- step_title: inventory-audio-modules
- summary: Captured a current-state inventory of the twelve committed `src/audio/` TypeScript modules (audioParity.ts, channels.ts, musParser.ts, musScheduler.ts, musicSystem.ts, oplRegisters.ts, oplSynth.ts, pcmMixer.ts, sfxLumps.ts, soundOrigins.ts, soundSystem.ts, spatial.ts) that model the vanilla DOOM 1.9 audio surface. The artefact `plan_vanilla_parity/current-state/inventory-audio-modules.json` is source-only metadata: per-module SHA-256 fingerprint, on-disk size and line count, exported interfaces/functions/constants/classes/types/const-enums, external imports (with duplicates preserved per the test's `externalImports` walker), src/test importer counts, role description, and a Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `vanilla_concept_modeled` anchor. Module groups partition the audio surface into four role buckets: audio_sfx (sfxLumps.ts, channels.ts, spatial.ts, soundOrigins.ts, soundSystem.ts, pcmMixer.ts) for the digital-sound-effect pipeline (DMX lump parsing, eight-channel allocator, S_AdjustSoundParams distance/pan, S_UpdateSounds per-tic update, S_StartSound entry point, and the i_sdlsound.c PCM resampler/mixer), audio_music (musParser.ts, musScheduler.ts, musicSystem.ts) for the MUS event grammar, MUS quicktick scheduler, and the S_StartMusic/S_ChangeMusic/S_StopMusic/S_PauseSound/S_ResumeSound/S_SetMusicVolume lifecycle, audio_opl_device (oplRegisters.ts, oplSynth.ts) for the OPL2 (YM3812) register file model and FM synthesis primitives that the i_oplmusic.c bridge drives, and audio_parity (audioParity.ts) for the cross-cutting AudioParityHarness composition that produces the AudioParityTicOutput stream consumed by the audio-hash oracle. The `reference_manifest_status` block cross-checks `reference/manifests/vanilla-limit-summary.json` (MAXPLAYERS=4, TICRATE=35, NUM_CHANNELS=8, NUMSFX=109, NUMMUSIC=68, MUSIC_VOLUME_MAX=127, MUS_TICKS_PER_GAME_TIC=4) and `reference/manifests/source-catalog.json` (Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `i_sound.c` and `s_sound.c` audio source files). Six implications are recorded: `musicSystem.ts` is the broadest export surface in the audio lane (10 src/ + 9 test/ importers) — reshaping MusicSystemState/MusicDeviceAction/SNDDEVICE_*/MUS_NONE/INTRO/INTROA/NUMMUSIC is a cross-lane breaking change; `audioParity.ts` composes every other audio module and is the AudioParityHarness contract for the audio-hash oracle (F-037); audio modules accept ChannelTable/MusicSystemState/MusSchedulerState/OplRegisterFile/AudioParityHarness records via injected parameters with the per-channel velocity cache being the only audio state with a hidden cross-loop dependency (vanilla mus2mid.c never resets channelvelocities[16] mid-song); NUMSFX=109/NUMMUSIC=68/MUSIC_VOLUME_MAX=127/NUM_CHANNELS=8/NORM_PRIORITY=64/NORM_PITCH=128/S_CLOSE_DIST=200*FRACUNIT/S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200*FRACUNIT/S_ATTENUATOR=1000/S_STEREO_SWING=96*FRACUNIT/NORM_SEP=128/BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME=15/BOSS_MAP_NUMBER=8/MUS_TICK_HZ=140/MUS_TICKS_PER_GAME_TIC=4/MUS_DEFAULT_VELOCITY=127/MUS_CHANNEL_COUNT=16 are bit-exact mirrors of vanilla doomdef.h/sounds.h/s_sound.c/mus2mid.c constants; OPL_NUM_CHANNELS=9/OPL_NUM_OPERATORS_PER_CHANNEL=2/OPL_REGISTER_FILE_SIZE=0x100/OPL_OPERATOR_OFFSETS table/OPL_SAMPLE_RATE_HZ=49716/OPL_PHASE_ACCUMULATOR_BITS=20/OPL_WAVEFORM_SAMPLES_PER_PERIOD=1024/OPL_MULTIPLIER_TABLE_X2 with the documented {10,10,12,12,15,15} duplicates/OPL_TL_DB_STEP=0.75 are bit-exact MAME/DOSBox YM3812 emulator invariants; SFX_HEADER_SIZE=8/SFX_FORMAT_DIGITAL=3/SFX_DEFAULT_SAMPLE_RATE=11025/SFX_LUMP_PREFIX='DS'/SFX_PADDING_BYTES=2/SFX_SILENCE_BYTE=0x80/PCM_BYTE_MIDPOINT=0x80/INT16_MIN=-32768/INT16_MAX=32767/MIX_MAX_VOLUME=127/SEP_LEFT_MAX=254/DEFAULT_OUTPUT_SAMPLE_RATE=44100/DMX_NATIVE_SAMPLE_RATE=11025/SOUND_UPDATE_LINK_MIN_VOLUME=1 are canonical i_sound.c/i_sdlsound.c values pinned for the SFX audio parity gate 11-030. The `follow_up_steps` array references thirty-seven downstream Phase 02/05/11/12 steps (02-013/02-014/02-032 audio oracle capture, 05-012/05-013 SFX/music lump parsing, 11-001..11-031 full audio implementation phase, 12-005 persist sound settings). The artefact does not embed proprietary WAD bytes — only source metadata, vanilla constants, and Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source-catalog anchors. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/current-state/inventory-audio-modules.test.ts` (22 tests, 453 expects) covering inventory artefact existence at the canonical write-locked path, canonical id/title/lane fields, the nine canonical required top-level fields in canonical order, summary/evidence-method content, captured_at_utc UTC ISO 8601 format, repository_root absolute path, source_directories enumeration with on-disk total recomputation, ASCII-sorted module ordering across the canonical twelve audio source paths, group partition into the four canonical role buckets, full module-entry fingerprint regeneration sweep (size_bytes, line_count, sha256, exported interfaces/functions/constants/classes/types/const-enums, external imports preserving duplicates, src/test importer counts via Bun.Glob), Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 anchor presence in `vanilla_concept_modeled`, external_imports ASCII-sort and on-disk existence enforcement, test_coverage matching `test/audio/`, reference_manifest_status cross-check against `vanilla-limit-summary.json` (MAXPLAYERS) and `source-catalog.json` (every named audio source file resolves), audio_boundary_status enumeration of every audio module with source-only metadata flag, implications cross-references (audio directory, MusicSystemState, AudioParityHarness, NUMSFX, follow-up step IDs), follow_up_steps pointer-to-real-step-file enforcement, step file write-lock declaration, and four failure-mode tests (music module misclassified as opl device, fabricated zero-sha256, tampered MAXPLAYERS limit, dropped audio test root). - open_risks: The inventory artefact pins exact SHA-256 fingerprints, exact on-disk byte counts, exact line counts, and exact src/test importer counts for all twelve `src/audio/` modules. Any future change to an audio module's bytes (formatter pass, semantic refactor, new export) will surface as a fingerprint mismatch in the focused test, requiring an inventory regeneration step. The `external_imports` field preserves duplicates (e.g. `audioParity.ts` lists `src/audio/channels.ts`, `src/audio/musicSystem.ts`, `src/audio/pcmMixer.ts`, `src/audio/soundOrigins.ts`, `src/audio/soundSystem.ts`, and `src/oracles/audioHash.ts` twice each because there are two distinct `import` statements from each module — one for type and one for runtime values), matching the inventory test's `externalImports` walker semantics; collapsing duplicates would silently desync this inventory from the test's expectation. The `reference_manifest_status` block cross-checks only MAXPLAYERS from `vanilla-limit-summary.json` because the manifest does not enumerate audio-specific limits (NUMSFX/NUMMUSIC/NUM_CHANNELS/MUSIC_VOLUME_MAX); the audio constants are pinned as primitive numeric fields (`ticrate_constant`, `num_channels_constant`, `num_sfx_constant`, `num_music_constant`, `music_volume_max_constant`, `mus_ticks_per_game_tic_constant`) without a manifest cross-check, so future audio inventory work that observes drift in these constants must update the inventory JSON. The mitigation pattern remains: (a) document the failures in `tests_run` as expected and outside this lane's write lock, (b) commit only this lane's own write-locked files plus plan-control updates, (c) await the inventory lane's snapshot regeneration as 01-005/01-006 are revisited and a future governance step un-flips the 01-010/03-008/03-009/05-007 step-file headings. The audio_boundary_status block records that audio modules accept state records via injected parameters; a future implementation step will need to wire the AudioParityHarness composition into the runtime `bun run doom.ts` entry point because the harness currently exists only as a parity oracle bridge rather than the live runtime audio system. Lane lock `49f80485-207a-47cf-8dbe-efa38bf6b262` is held by the launcher and will be released on normal exit. - step_title: parse-flat-namespace
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 flat namespace parser, the `R_InitFlats` pipeline that resolves the contiguous block of 64x64 palette-indexed floor and ceiling textures between the F_START and F_END markers in a WAD directory and assigns each entry a sequential firstflat-relative flat number that the renderer indexes through `flattranslation` at draw time. Wrote `src/assets/parse-flat-namespace.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger module that exports `FLAT_LUMP_BYTES = 4096` and a frozen `parseFlatNamespace(directory)` parser whose returned `FlatNamespace` exposes `startMarkerIndex`, `endMarkerIndex`, `firstFlatIndex` (= startMarkerIndex + 1, the vanilla `firstflat` formula), `lastFlatIndex` (= endMarkerIndex - 1, the vanilla `lastflat` formula), `numFlats` (= lastFlatIndex - firstFlatIndex + 1, the vanilla `numflats` formula), `flatTranslationSlotCount` (= numFlats + 1, the vanilla `Z_Malloc((numflats+1)*sizeof(*flattranslation))` slot count), `flatTranslationIdentity` (a frozen length-numFlats identity array `[0, 1, ..., numFlats-1]` mirroring the vanilla `for (i=0;i<numflats;i++) flattranslation[i] = i;` loop), and `entries` (a frozen length-numFlats array of frozen `FlatNamespaceEntry` records each carrying `name`, `directoryIndex`, `flatNumber = directoryIndex - firstFlatIndex`, and `isInnerMarker` flagging the inner sub-markers F1_START/F1_END/F2_START/F2_END/F3_START/F3_END). The parser throws an `Error` when F_START or F_END is missing or when F_END does not strictly follow F_START. A companion `flatNumForName(namespace, name)` helper mirrors vanilla `R_FlatNumForName` (uppercase comparison, eight-byte truncation, `i - firstflat` return formula, fatal `I_Error` on miss). The audit module exports a fourteen-entry `FLAT_NAMESPACE_AUDIT` ledger pinning the verbatim Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source lines from `src/doom/r_data.c`'s `R_InitFlats`, `R_FlatNumForName`, and `R_InitData` against the runtime contract, plus the inner-submarker-counting axis (F1_START gets flat number 0, F1_END gets flat number 55 in shareware DOOM1.WAD), the 4096-byte flat pixel size axis, the shareware-DOOM1-fifty-six-flats axis, and the cache-by-directory-num axis. A sixteen-entry `FLAT_NAMESPACE_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` ledger pins the cross-axis identities (numflats formula, firstflat = start + 1, lastflat = end - 1, flattranslation slot count = numflats + 1, identity-init loop, frozen namespace return, sequential flat numbers, directoryIndex = firstflat + flatNumber, three rejection modes, flatNumForName return formula, flatNumForName throws on miss, FLAT_LUMP_BYTES = 4096, and the every-axis-declared meta invariant). The `crossCheckFlatNamespaceRuntime(snapshot)` cross-check accepts a `FlatNamespaceRuntimeSnapshot` and returns `derived:<id>` and `audit:<id>:not-observed` failure identifiers; the live runtime snapshot reports zero failures. A four-entry `SHAREWARE_DOOM1_WAD_FLAT_NAMESPACE_ORACLE.pinnedFlats` array pins the local `doom/DOOM1.WAD` flat facts: FLOOR0_1 at directory index 1208 / flat number 1 / file offset 3954612 / size 4096 / sha256 `1e366315627e56a8f664aeb1d2f0eceeb4f4f83020b8aa5feb56db31199822d7`; FLOOR4_8 at directory index 1217 / flat number 10 / file offset 3991476 / size 4096 / sha256 `0c68cce54da0d406a6ef20293f9b9817b987f6d8832ac64bdf4c4c18657d5703`; NUKAGE1 at directory index 1258 / flat number 51 / file offset 4159412 / size 4096 / sha256 `727dbc3a3439067fda299a818910a292eab7f8dc8b78152b7ba977e6f707811f`; F_SKY1 at directory index 1261 / flat number 54 / file offset 4171700 / size 4096 / sha256 `203225b7cc9ceea3817af1d9b0ce4eea8fb230734e75ada272d86d2e893c8d85`. - summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 `D_DoomMain` init-order skeleton from id Software's `linuxdoom-1.10/d_main.c` as a self-contained audit ledger module. The canonical surface is the verbatim sequence of twelve `printf("X_Init: ...\n"); X_Init();` pairs interleaved through the second half of `D_DoomMain`, partitioned 4 + 8 across the gamemode-derived banner block: the four pre-banner steps fire in the order V_Init → M_LoadDefaults → Z_Init → W_InitMultipleFiles, and the eight post-banner steps fire in the order M_Init → R_Init → P_Init → I_Init → D_CheckNetGame → S_Init → HU_Init → ST_Init. Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-d-doommain-init-order-skeleton.ts` exporting `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_INIT_ORDER` (twelve frozen `VanillaInitStep` entries with verbatim `cSymbol`, verbatim `stdoutLine`, and `pre-banner`/`post-banner` phase classification), `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_INIT_STEP_COUNT = 12`, `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_PRE_BANNER_STEP_COUNT = 4`, `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_POST_BANNER_STEP_COUNT = 8`, and `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_ABSENT_CHOCOLATE_SYMBOLS = ['OPL_Init', 'NET_Init', 'I_InitStretchTables']` with `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_ABSENT_CHOCOLATE_SYMBOL_COUNT = 3`. The audit ledger pins twenty-one contract clauses against `d_main.c::D_DoomMain`: a 12-step count, the 4 + 8 partition, twelve per-position pins (each citing the exact cSymbol and verbatim printf literal — including the trailing-space idiosyncrasy on Z_Init's "Z_Init: Init zone memory allocation daemon. \n" and the leading-newline idiosyncrasy on P_Init's "\nP_Init: Init Playloop state.\n" that breaks the R_Init progress-dot line), three Chocolate-only-omission clauses (OPL_Init / NET_Init / I_InitStretchTables), one verbatim-literal clause covering all twelve printf strings, and three divergence-from-Chocolate clauses (the V_Init/M_LoadDefaults/Z_Init pre-banner reorder vs Chocolate's Z_Init/V_Init/M_LoadDefaults order, the I_Init-after-P_Init position vs Chocolate's I_Init-after-W_Init position, and the D_CheckNetGame-precedes-S_Init order vs Chocolate's reverse order). A twelve-entry `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_INIT_ORDER_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` ledger pins the cross-cutting parity rules. A 29-entry `VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_INIT_ORDER_PROBES` ledger covers nine query kinds (symbol-at-index, index-of-symbol, symbol-presence, symbol-stdout-line, symbol-phase, symbol-precedes, sequence-length, pre-banner-step-count, post-banner-step-count) — twelve symbol-at-index probes covering every canonical position, three symbol-presence probes for OPL_Init/NET_Init/I_InitStretchTables-absent plus one V_Init-positive-control, two index-of-symbol probes (ST_Init=11, OPL_Init=-1), three symbol-stdout-line probes pinning the trailing-space/no-trailing-newline/leading-newline idiosyncrasies, two symbol-phase probes, two symbol-precedes probes (P_Init→I_Init and D_CheckNetGame→S_Init divergence pins), three count probes (12 / 4 / 8), and one absent-precedence probe (OPL_Init does NOT precede ST_Init because OPL_Init is absent). The `crossCheckVanillaDDoomMainInitOrder(handler)` cross-check accepts a `VanillaDDoomMainInitOrderHandler` (single `runProbe` method returning a `VanillaDDoomMainInitOrderResult` with seven nullable answer fields) and returns failure ids of the form `probe:<id>:<answeredFieldName>:value-mismatch`. The `REFERENCE_VANILLA_D_DOOMMAIN_INIT_ORDER_HANDLER` walks the canonical sequence and answers every probe correctly. A `deriveExpectedVanillaDDoomMainInitOrderResult(probe)` helper exposes the reference handler for synthetic-probe cross-validation. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-d-doommain-init-order-skeleton.test.ts` (79 tests, 472 expects) covering ledger shape (count, uniqueness, references), per-clause content (every clause names the right symbols and idiosyncrasies), canonical-sequence shape (12 entries, 4 + 8 partition, no interleaving, verbatim Z_Init trailing-space / R_Init no-newline / P_Init leading-newline, ST_Init at index 11), absent-Chocolate-symbol list (3 entries OPL_Init/NET_Init/I_InitStretchTables, none present in canonical order), derived-invariant list (12 entries with unique ids), probe-set shape (29 entries with consistent query/expected pairs and witness-invariant cross-references), reference-handler cross-check (zero failures, every query kind answered correctly), fifteen failure-mode handlers (Z_Init at index 0, I_Init at index 4, swapped D_CheckNetGame/S_Init, includes-OPL_Init, includes-NET_Init, appends-I_InitStretchTables, drops-Z_Init-trailing-space, adds-R_Init-trailing-newline, drops-P_Init-leading-newline, V_Init-misclassified-as-post-banner, sequence-length-15, pre-banner-step-count-3, swapped-M_LoadDefaults/Z_Init, ST_Init-before-HU_Init, OPL_Init-precedes-ST_Init), the deriveExpected helper sanity (out-of-range index, unknown symbol, absent-precedence-returns-false), reconstructed-stdout-stream tests (12 lines covering canonical symbols in order, I_Init after P_Init, D_CheckNetGame before S_Init, V_Init before Z_Init, no Chocolate-only stdout literals), and step-file format checks (declares `lane: launch`, both write-locked paths, the five research sources d_main.c/g_game.c/i_timer.c/i_video.c/m_menu.c, and the prerequisite gate 00-018).

These are linuxdoom-1.10 source idiosyncrasies that survive into vanilla 1.9 and any cross-platform port that pulls Chocolate Doom 2.2.1's stdout strings verbatim will silently break the vanilla stdout fingerprint (Chocolate's literals match vanilla's for the 12 shared symbols, but Chocolate's order interleaves three additional X_Init lines and prints them in a different order). Because no runtime D_DoomMain skeleton exists yet, this audit is purely declarative — a future implementation step (03-009 or later) will need to build a runtime that emits these twelve stdout literals in this exact order and a later oracle-capture step will need to compare against a captured `doom/DOOMD.EXE` startup transcript to confirm the vanilla DOS executable produces the same fingerprint. ## 2026-04-27 - 05-006 parse-patch-picture-format

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: wad
- lock_id: 5ef57989-3406-4944-8542-629535aab4f1
- step_id: 05-006
- step_title: parse-patch-picture-format
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 `patch_t` / `post_t` picture lump byte format against verbatim Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 declarations from `src/doom/r_defs.h` (the `patch_t` and `post_t` struct declarations) and `src/doom/v_video.c` (the `V_DrawPatch` body, including the `y -= SHORT(patch->topoffset)`, `x -= SHORT(patch->leftoffset)`, `column = (column_t *)((byte *)patch + LONG(patch->columnofs[col]))`, `source = (byte *)column + 3`, and `column = (column_t *)( (byte *)column + column->length + 4)` lines that fix the byte arithmetic). Wrote `src/assets/parse-patch-picture-format.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger module that exports the runtime constants `PATCH_HEADER_BYTES = 8`, `PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES = 4`, `POST_HEADER_BYTES = 3`, `POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES = 1`, `POST_OVERHEAD_BYTES = 4`, `PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER = 0xff`, plus a frozen `parsePatchPicture(buffer)` parser whose returned `DecodedPatchPicture` exposes a frozen header (`width`, `height`, `leftOffset`, `topOffset` all signed int16 LE), a frozen columns array of length `width`, each column itself a frozen array of frozen posts whose `pixels` are live `Uint8Array` views into the source buffer (no copy). The parser throws `RangeError` on a buffer smaller than the 8-byte header, on a buffer too small for the `width * 4` column-offset table, on an out-of-range `columnofs[i]` value, and on a post `length` that would push the pixel run past the end of the buffer. The audit module exports an eighteen-entry `PATCH_PICTURE_FORMAT_AUDIT` ledger pinning eight `patch_t` axes (header bytes 8, width int16 LE, height int16 LE, leftoffset signed int16 LE, topoffset signed int16 LE, column-offset stride 4, columnofs int32 LE, columnofs absolute from lump start), six `post_t` / `V_DrawPatch` axes (post topdelta byte, post length byte, post leading pad byte, post trailing pad byte, post total overhead 4 bytes, post end marker 0xff), two draw-arithmetic axes (y subtracts topoffset, x subtracts leftoffset), the shareware-DOOM1-uses-single-topdelta-encoding axis, and the cache-by-name-via-W_CacheLumpName axis. A thirteen-entry `PATCH_PICTURE_FORMAT_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` ledger pins the cross-lane identities (PATCH_HEADER_BYTES = 4*int16, PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES = int32, POST_HEADER_BYTES = 3, POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES = 1, POST_OVERHEAD_TOTAL = 4, PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER = 0xff, parsePatchPicture returns frozen header and columns, header fields are int16, four parser failure modes, and the every-axis-declared meta invariant). The `crossCheckPatchPictureFormatRuntime(snapshot)` cross-check accepts a `PatchPictureFormatRuntimeSnapshot` and returns `derived:<id>` and `audit:<id>:not-observed` failure identifiers; the live runtime snapshot reports zero failures. A three-entry `SHAREWARE_DOOM1_WAD_PATCH_ORACLE` pins the local `doom/DOOM1.WAD` patch facts: TITLEPIC at directory index 235, file offset 1933024, size 68168, dimensions 320x200, both offsets 0, sha256 `f2cfb4e8e2f80aaad1203b1209e3e0cfb83eebe8d48ab1e276a8a60907808b9c`, column-zero post count 2; STFST00 at directory index 361, file offset 2042632, size 808, dimensions 24x29, leftOffset -5 / topOffset -2 (proves the runtime decoder preserves the int16 sign bit), sha256 `afb4862b80030350df5ac2ce52735b250a20d367cb53a035628ce0e6330e7399`, column-zero post count 1; AMMNUM0 at directory index 236, file offset 2001192, size 48, dimensions 3x5, leftOffset -1 / topOffset 0, sha256 `b9f4bf453aaefbf4cc2631e1047cf879a249bd9d3b79c265874eb49159504cca`, column-zero post count 1. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/wad/parse-patch-picture-format.test.ts` (62 tests, 249 expects) covering audit-ledger shape, derived invariant ids, runtime constant agreement, parser runtime contracts (frozen views over the source buffer, RangeError rejection on each malformed input case, multi-post column ordering, exact `length + 4` post-overhead arithmetic), live runtime snapshot cross-check, thirteen failure-mode tampers (PATCH_HEADER_BYTES, PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES, POST_HEADER_BYTES, POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES, POST_OVERHEAD_BYTES, PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER, parserReturnsFrozenOuter, parserPreservesNegativeLeftOffset, parserPreservesNegativeTopOffset, four parser-rejection tampers, and an equivalent-snapshot baseline), shareware DOOM1.WAD oracle byte-level evidence (per-patch directory-index / file-offset / size / dimensions / sign-preserving offsets / sha256 / column-zero post-count probes plus the manifest cross-check that `lumpCategories.patch === 165`), seven oracle failure-mode tampers, and step-file format checks (declares `lane: wad`, both write-locked paths, and `r_data.c` / `w_wad.c` / `p_setup.c` as research sources).

## 2026-04-27 - 04-006 audit-fine-tangent-and-slope-tables

- status: completed

- summary: Pinned the operational semantics of the vanilla DOOM 1.9 fine-tangent (`finetangent[FINEANGLES/2]`) and slope (`tantoangle[SLOPERANGE+1]` plus `SlopeDiv(unsigned num, unsigned den)`) tables one level deeper than the prior 04-005 audit, which captured the static layout, byte-level fingerprints, and cardinal probe values of every trig table. Wrote `src/core/audit-fine-tangent-and-slope-tables.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from any sibling `src/core/` module — the audited BAM endpoint `0x20000000` and every probe expectation are hardcoded as literals so a corruption of either runtime module cannot also calibrate the probe table that detects the corruption. The audit module exports fifteen hand-pinned canonical constants (finetangent min/pivot/half-bound/FRACUNIT-crossing values; tantoangle first/middle/final increment values plus the cumulative ANG45 sum; slope guard threshold/shifts) plus two sha256 fingerprints mirrored from 04-005 so a transcription drift in either ledger fails loudly. A ten-entry `FINE_TANGENT_AND_SLOPE_AUDIT` ledger pins the Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source lines for three `c-header` facts (the verbatim `extern fixed_t finetangent[FINEANGLES/2];`, `extern angle_t tantoangle[SLOPERANGE+1];`, `int SlopeDiv (unsigned num, unsigned den);` declarations from `src/tables.h`) and seven `c-body` facts (the verbatim array-literal openers/closers for both tables and the verbatim `SlopeDiv` guard / formula / clamp from `src/tables.c`). A thirteen-entry `FINE_TANGENT_AND_SLOPE_INVARIANTS` ledger pins the operational invariants that go DEEPER than 04-005's broad-table checks: finetangent strict-monotonic increase, sign bipartition at index 2048, no exact zero, exact pivot values, exact FRACUNIT-crossing pair, tantoangle strict-monotonic increase, increment sum equals exactly ANG45, increments monotonically non-strictly decreasing reflecting arctangent concavity, slopeDiv returns value in [0, SLOPERANGE], guard exact at den < 512, composition `tantoangle[slopeDiv]` always lands in [0, ANG45], and table-buffer hash invariants. A sixteen-entry `FINE_TANGENT_AND_SLOPE_PROBES` ledger covers four targets: six finetangent probes (strict-increase sentinels at indices 1 and 4094, antisymmetry-pivot values at 2047 and 2048, FRACUNIT-crossing pair at 3071 and 3072), three tantoangle increment probes anchoring arctangent curvature (333772 / 267072 / 166912 at indices 0 / 1023 / 2047), four slopeDiv guard-boundary and uint32-coercion probes, and three composition probes (zero-slope yields BAM 0, unit-slope yields ANG45, quarter-slope yields BAM 167458912 which is larger than the linearised ANG45/4 = 134217728 because of arctangent concavity). The `crossCheckFineTangentAndSlope(candidate)` cross-check accepts any `{finetangent, tantoangle, slopeDiv}` tuple and returns a `readonly string[]` of `probe:<id>` and `invariant:<id>` failure identifiers; the live runtime tuple reports zero failures. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-fine-tangent-and-slope-tables.test.ts` (81 tests, 1.65M expects) covering audited canonical constants vs hand-pinned literals, fact ledger shape (closed at exactly ten entries with three c-header + seven c-body), invariant ledger shape (closed at thirteen entries), probe ledger shape (closed at sixteen entries with all four targets covered), audited sha256 fingerprints match the live runtime tables, per-probe runtime values match expectations, runtime invariants for finetangent / tantoangle / slopeDiv / composition (including a Cartesian sweep of 8192 first-octant inputs verifying BAM ∈ [0, ANG45]), cross-check on the live runtime tuple reports zero failures, eleven failure-mode tests, sha256OfTypedArray helper sanity, and step-file format checks.

## 2026-04-27 - 03-007 implement-doom-game-mode-detection

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: launch
- lock_id: 529315aa-a3eb-444c-aad8-4cde23bce0c6
- step_id: 03-007
- step_title: implement-doom-game-mode-detection
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 game-mode detection surface (the `gamemode_t` enum derivation) inside `IdentifyVersion()` against id Software linuxdoom-1.10 `doomdef.h` (the five-literal `gamemode_t` enum) and `d_main.c` (the seven `if (!access(name,R_OK))` candidate blocks plus the closing `printf("Game mode indeterminate.\n"); gamemode = indetermined; return;` indeterminate fallback). The vanilla 1.9 enum has exactly five values: `shareware`, `registered`, `commercial`, `retail`, `indetermined` — the typo (missing `a`, dictionary spelling is `indeterminate`) is a deliberate parity invariant preserved verbatim by the runtime `GameMode` literal-union type in `src/bootstrap/gameMode.ts`. The candidate-filename → gamemode mapping is many-to-one for `commercial` (four filenames: `doom2f.wad`, `doom2.wad`, `plutonia.wad`, `tnt.wad`) and one-to-one for `retail`/`registered`/`shareware` (`doomu.wad`/`doom.wad`/`doom1.wad`). Vanilla 1.9 predates the Freedoom community IWAD project, the HACX/Chex Quest TC IWADs, and the Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `D_IdentifyIWADByContents` lump-based fallback; none of `freedoom1.wad`/`freedoom2.wad`/`freedm.wad`/`hacx.wad`/`chex.wad` are recognised by vanilla `IdentifyVersion()`. Vanilla `IdentifyVersion()` does NOT inspect WAD lump contents to derive gamemode (no `W_CheckNumForName`, no `W_GetNumForName`, no header-byte inspection); the matched filename is the sole determinant. On no-match, vanilla prints `"Game mode indeterminate.\n"` to stdout via `printf()`, assigns `gamemode = indetermined;`, and returns normally — does NOT call `I_Error` to abort startup (Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 diverges by erroring out instead). Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-doom-game-mode-detection.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from any runtime IWAD-selection module (only the `GameMode` literal-union type from `src/bootstrap/gameMode.ts` is imported) so a corrupted runtime cannot silently calibrate the audit's own probe table. The audit module exports a thirteen-entry `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_DETECTION_CONTRACT_AUDIT` ledger pinning the verbatim `d_main.c`/`IdentifyVersion` and `doomdef.h`/`gamemode_t` clauses, a frozen seven-entry `VANILLA_CANDIDATE_FILENAME_TO_GAME_MODE_MAP` list with candidateFilename/gameMode/probeOrderIndex per entry, six pinned constants (`VANILLA_CANDIDATE_FILENAME_COUNT = 7`, `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_ENUM_VALUE_COUNT = 5`, `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_ENUM_VALUES`, `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_INDETERMINATE_PRINTOUT_LITERAL = 'Game mode indeterminate.\n'`, `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_INDETERMINATE_ENUM_LITERAL = 'indetermined'`, `VANILLA_UNRECOGNISED_IWAD_FILENAMES = ['freedoom1.wad', 'freedoom2.wad', 'freedm.wad', 'hacx.wad', 'chex.wad']`), a fifteen-entry `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_DETECTION_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` ledger, and a seventeen-entry `VANILLA_GAME_MODE_DETECTION_PROBES` ledger covering each of the seven canonical filenames individually, the empty-search-directory indeterminate path, the precedence rules between doomu.wad/doom.wad and doom.wad/doom1.wad, the doom2f.wad/doom2.wad first-match rule, the all-seven-present case, the Freedoom-only and freedm-only no-match cases, the hacx+chex no-match case, the doom1.wad+freedoom1.wad coexistence pinning shareware, and the plutonia.wad+tnt.wad first-match rule. The `crossCheckVanillaGameModeDetection(handler)` cross-check accepts any `VanillaGameModeDetectionHandler` and returns a `readonly string[]` of stable failure identifiers (`probe:<id>:matchedFilename:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:gameMode:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:indeterminatePrintoutFired:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:probedSequence:length-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:probedSequence:order-mismatch`); the canonical reference handler reports zero failures. A `deriveExpectedVanillaGameModeDetectionResult(presentCandidateFilenames)` helper mirrors the canonical scan (Set-based presence test, walk in canonical probe order, stop at first match) so the focused test can cross-validate every probe expectation independently. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-doom-game-mode-detection.test.ts` (80 tests, 559 expects) covering ledger shape, constants, per-clause content checks, probe-shape invariants, reference handler cross-check (zero failures plus per-candidate regression tests for all 13 probe ids), nine failure-mode handlers (wrong gameMode swap, retail-as-registered swap, printout-always-false, aborts-on-no-match, recognises-Freedoom-as-commercial, highest-rank-wins (reverse-order walk), only-checks-doom1 short-circuit, reordered probe sequence, doom2.wad-mismaps-as-retail), `deriveExpectedVanillaGameModeDetectionResult` helper sanity, four behavioral consistency checks, and three step-file format checks (declares `lane: launch`, names both write-locked paths, lists the five canonical research sources `d_main.c`/`g_game.c`/`i_timer.c`/`i_video.c`/`m_menu.c`, declares prerequisite gate `00-018`).

## 2026-04-27 - 03-006 implement-user-supplied-iwad-selection

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: launch
- lock_id: 529315aa-a3eb-444c-aad8-4cde23bce0c6
- step_id: 03-006
- step_title: implement-user-supplied-iwad-selection
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 user-supplied IWAD selection surface inside `IdentifyVersion()` against id Software linuxdoom-1.10 `d_main.c`. The canonical mechanism is the developer-mode parameter triple `-shdev` / `-regdev` / `-comdev`: each parameter overrides the seven-candidate `access(R_OK)` scan by setting gamemode to a literal enum, setting the `devparm` global to true, calling `D_AddFile` against a hardcoded `DEVDATA"<basename>"` literal that bypasses `getenv("DOOMWADDIR")`, copying `DEVDATA"default.cfg"` into `basedefault`, and early-returning. Vanilla 1.9 has NO `-iwad <path>` flag (a Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 addition via `D_FindIWAD`/`M_CheckParmWithArgs("-iwad", 1)`), and `-file` adds PWADs without affecting gamemode or IWAD selection. Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-user-supplied-iwad-selection.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from any runtime IWAD-selection module (so a corrupted runtime cannot calibrate the audit's own probe table). The audit module exports an eleven-entry `VANILLA_USER_SUPPLIED_IWAD_SELECTION_CONTRACT_AUDIT` ledger pinning the verbatim `d_main.c`/`IdentifyVersion` clauses (`DEV_PARAMETER_NAMES_ARE_FIXED_TRIPLE`, `DEV_PARAMETER_PROBE_ORDER_IS_SHDEV_REGDEV_COMDEV`, `DEV_PARAMETER_TRIPLE_PROBES_PRECEDE_CANDIDATE_SCAN`, `DEV_PARAMETER_PINS_GAME_MODE_BY_FLAG_NAME`, `DEV_PARAMETER_SETS_DEVPARM_GLOBAL_TRUE`, `DEV_PARAMETER_USES_HARDCODED_DEVDATA_BASENAME`, `DEV_PARAMETER_SHORT_CIRCUITS_CANDIDATE_SCAN_VIA_RETURN`, `DEV_PARAMETER_OVERWRITES_BASEDEFAULT_PATH_LITERAL`, `NO_DASH_IWAD_FLAG_EXISTS_IN_VANILLA_ONE_DOT_NINE`, `DASH_FILE_FLAG_DOES_NOT_OVERRIDE_GAME_MODE`, `DEV_PARAMETER_M_CHECKPARM_LOOKUP_IS_CASE_INSENSITIVE`), a frozen three-entry `VANILLA_DEVELOPER_MODE_PARAMETERS` list with parameterName/gameMode/devDataBasename/probeOrderIndex per entry, four pinned constants (`VANILLA_NONEXISTENT_DASH_IWAD_PARAMETER_NAME = '-iwad'`, `VANILLA_DASH_FILE_PARAMETER_NAME = '-file'`, `VANILLA_DEVELOPER_MODE_DEFAULT_CFG_BASENAME = 'default.cfg'`, `VANILLA_DEVELOPER_MODE_PARAMETER_COUNT = 3`), a ten-entry `VANILLA_USER_SUPPLIED_IWAD_SELECTION_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` ledger (TRIPLE_HAS_EXACTLY_THREE_FLAGS, TRIPLE_ORDER_IS_VERBATIM_VANILLA, PINS_GAME_MODE_BY_FLAG_NAME_ALONE, SETS_DEVPARM_FLAG_TRUE, LOADS_HARDCODED_DEVDATA_BASENAME_NOT_DOOMWADDIR, OVERRIDE_BYPASSES_CANDIDATE_SCAN, FIRST_MATCH_WINS, OVERWRITES_BASEDEFAULT_WITH_DEVDATA_DEFAULT_CFG, DASH_IWAD_FLAG_IS_NOT_RECOGNISED_BY_VANILLA, DASH_FILE_FLAG_DOES_NOT_AFFECT_GAME_MODE_OR_IWAD_SELECTION), and a thirteen-entry `VANILLA_USER_SUPPLIED_IWAD_SELECTION_PROBES` ledger covering each developer-mode parameter individually, the no-match indeterminate fallback, the precedence rules between -shdev/-regdev/-comdev, the devparm flag toggle, the hardcoded basename rule, the candidate-scan bypass, the basedefault overwrite, the unrecognised -iwad flag, and the -file passthrough behavior with and without a dev-mode flag. The `crossCheckVanillaUserSuppliedIwadSelection(handler)` cross-check accepts any `VanillaUserSuppliedIwadSelectionHandler` and returns a `readonly string[]` of stable failure identifiers (`probe:<id>:matchedParameterName:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:gameMode:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:devparmFlag:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:devDataBasename:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:probedSequence:length-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:probedSequence:order-mismatch`); the canonical reference handler reports zero failures. A `deriveExpectedUserSuppliedIwadSelectionResult(virtualCommandLine)` helper mirrors `M_CheckParm` semantics (case-insensitive scan, index >= 1 to skip program name) so the focused test can cross-validate every probe expectation independently. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-user-supplied-iwad-selection.test.ts` (68 tests, 428 expects) covering ledger shape (eleven contract clauses, ten derived invariants, thirteen probes; every id unique; every clause references `d_main.c` and pins `IdentifyVersion`), constants (each developer-mode parameter's frozen gameMode/devDataBasename/probeOrderIndex, the four module-level constants, the disjoint-flag set assertion), per-clause content checks (each invariant cites the canonical C strings: -shdev/-regdev/-comdev names, -shdev/-regdev/-comdev order, doom2f.wad as the first candidate, -shdev → shareware/-regdev → registered/-comdev → commercial pairings, devparm/true, "-shdev → \"doom1.wad\""/"-regdev → \"doom.wad\""/"-comdev → \"doom2.wad\"" pairings, DEVDATA, DOOMWADDIR, return;, access(R_OK), strcpy, basedefault, default.cfg, -iwad, Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 / D_FindIWAD divergence note, -file/D_DoomMain/D_AddFile/PWAD distinction, M_CheckParm/strcasecmp), probe-shape invariants (every probe ends at the matched parameter or runs all three probes, every expected probe sequence is a prefix of the canonical three-parameter order, every gameMode/devDataBasename/devparmFlag is consistent with the matched parameter, every probe expectation matches `deriveExpectedUserSuppliedIwadSelectionResult`), reference handler cross-check (zero failures plus per-parameter regression tests for -shdev/-regdev/-comdev/no-flag/-iwad/-file/file+shdev), eight failure-mode handlers (wrong gameMode, devparm-always-false, wrong basename, reordered triple, recognises -iwad as a dev-mode flag, -file overrides gameMode, dev-mode runs full scan, short-circuited probe sequence, reordered probe sequence), `deriveExpectedUserSuppliedIwadSelectionResult` helper sanity (empty CL, -shdev CL, -comdev CL, case-insensitive -SHDEV CL, program-name argument at index 0 ignored, -iwad CL ignored), three behavioral consistency checks (every dev parameter short-circuits the candidate scan, removing the dev parameter drops back to indetermined, combining -iwad with -shdev still pins shareware), and three step-file format checks (declares `lane: launch`, names both write-locked paths, lists the five canonical research sources `d_main.c`/`g_game.c`/`i_timer.c`/`i_video.c`/`m_menu.c`, declares prerequisite gate `00-018`).

## 2026-04-26 - 04-005 audit-trig-lookup-tables

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: core
- lock_id: 8e8565ef-3f37-4d3c-a83f-b7599f0d1e20
- step_id: 04-005
- step_title: audit-trig-lookup-tables
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 trigonometric lookup tables (`finetangent[FINEANGLES/2]`, `finesine[5*FINEANGLES/4]`, the `finecosine` pointer alias `&finesine[FINEANGLES/4]`, `tantoangle[SLOPERANGE+1]`) and the `SlopeDiv(unsigned num, unsigned den)` helper from `src/core/trig.ts` against the canonical Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 declarations in `src/tables.h` and `src/tables.c`. Wrote `src/core/audit-trig-lookup-tables.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from `src/core/trig.ts` (so a corruption in trig.ts cannot silently corrupt the probe table that detects the corruption). The audit module exports thirteen hand-pinned canonical constants (`AUDITED_FINEANGLES = 8192`, `AUDITED_FINEMASK = 8191`, `AUDITED_ANGLETOFINESHIFT = 19`, `AUDITED_SLOPERANGE = 2048`, `AUDITED_SLOPEBITS = 11`, `AUDITED_DBITS = 5`, `AUDITED_FINETANGENT_LENGTH = 4096`, `AUDITED_FINESINE_LENGTH = 10240`, `AUDITED_FINECOSINE_OFFSET = 2048`, `AUDITED_FINECOSINE_LENGTH = 8192`, `AUDITED_TANTOANGLE_LENGTH = 2049`, `AUDITED_FINETANGENT_PEAK_MAGNITUDE = 170910304`, `AUDITED_FINESINE_PEAK_MAGNITUDE = 65535`, `AUDITED_TANTOANGLE_AT_SLOPERANGE = 0x20000000`) plus four sha256 fingerprints (`AUDITED_FINETANGENT_SHA256` `8988638b...e521a031`, `AUDITED_FINESINE_SHA256` `a2a1181e...728a2ebb`, `AUDITED_FINECOSINE_SHA256` `ec1f6386...a8f85cbf`, `AUDITED_TANTOANGLE_SHA256` `ba4346ce...9dee7e11`) capturing the canonical little-endian Typed-Array byte layouts. A ten-entry `TRIG_LOOKUP_AUDIT` ledger pins the Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source lines for eight `c-header` facts (`#define FINEANGLES              8192`, `#define FINEMASK                (FINEANGLES-1)`, `#define ANGLETOFINESHIFT        19`, `#define SLOPERANGE      2048`, `extern fixed_t finetangent[FINEANGLES/2];`, `extern fixed_t finesine[5*FINEANGLES/4];`, `extern fixed_t *finecosine;`, `extern angle_t tantoangle[SLOPERANGE+1];` — all from `src/tables.h`) and two `c-body` facts (the `fixed_t *finecosine = &finesine[FINEANGLES/4];` pointer-alias initialiser and the verbatim `SlopeDiv(unsigned num, unsigned den) { unsigned ans; if (den < 512) return SLOPERANGE; ans = (num<<3)/(den>>8); return ans <= SLOPERANGE ? ans : SLOPERANGE; }` body — both from `src/tables.c`). A ten-entry `TRIG_LOOKUP_INVARIANTS` ledger pins the derived parity invariants (FINETANGENT/FINESINE/FINECOSINE/TANTOANGLE length checks, FINETANGENT antisymmetric across midpoint `finetangent[i] === -finetangent[4095 - i]`, |finesine[i]| <= FRACUNIT - 1 = 65535, finecosine[i] === finesine[i + 2048] zero-copy alias, tantoangle non-decreasing, tantoangle endpoints (0, ANG45), all four table buffer sha256 fingerprints match the audited values). A 25-entry `TRIG_LOOKUP_PROBES` ledger covers five tables/sites (finetangent endpoints + antisymmetry pivots + first index, finesine cardinal points + clipping peaks + extension tail, finecosine cardinal points verifying the alias semantics, tantoangle endpoints + mid-points, SlopeDiv divide-by-zero + unit-slope corner cases). The `crossCheckTrigLookupTables(candidate)` cross-check accepts any candidate `{finetangent, finesine, finecosine, tantoangle, slopeDiv}` tuple and returns a `readonly string[]` of `probe:<id>` and `invariant:<id>` failure identifiers; the live runtime tuple reports zero failures. A `sha256OfTypedArray(view)` helper hashes typed-array byte buffers in their canonical little-endian layout and is used both at fact-pinning time and inside the cross-check. Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-trig-lookup-tables.test.ts` (68 tests, 24876 expects) covering: audited canonical constants vs runtime exports vs hand-pinned literals; fact ledger shape (closed at exactly ten entries with eight c-header + two c-body, every id unique, every description and cReference non-empty, every c-header fact references `src/tables.h` and every c-body fact references `src/tables.c`); fact ledger values (each fact pins the verbatim canonical Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source line including spacing); invariant ledger shape (closed at exactly ten entries, every id unique); probe ledger shape (closed at exactly twenty-five entries, every id unique, every note non-empty, every table covered, every table-indexed input is a valid in-range integer index, every slopeDiv input is a (num, den) pair); audited sha256 fingerprints match the live runtime tables (one test per table); per-probe runtime values match the canonical expectations (single sweep over all 25 probes); runtime invariants (finetangent antisymmetric across all 4096 cells, |finesine[i]| <= 65535 across all 10240 cells, both ±65535 peaks actually appear in the table, ±170910304 finetangent peaks appear at the half-circle endpoints, finecosine[i] === finesine[i + 2048] across all 8192 cells, finecosine shares the same `ArrayBuffer` as finesine via TypedArray subarray view with the correct byteOffset, tantoangle non-decreasing across all 2049 cells, tantoangle endpoints are 0 and ANG45); cross-check on the live runtime tuple reports zero failures; failure-mode tests (corrupted finetangent buffer at index 0 detected by probe + antisymmetry + hash invariants; finesine peak above FRACUNIT - 1 detected by probe + peak-magnitude + hash invariants; finecosine recomputed independently and drifting from finesine detected by probe + alias + hash invariants; tantoangle non-monotonic detected by probe + monotonicity + hash invariants; tantoangle endpoint not equal to ANG45 detected by probe + endpoints + hash invariants; slopeDiv that bypasses the `< 512` guard detected by the divide-by-zero probe; finetangent length mismatch detected by length + hash invariants); sha256OfTypedArray helper sanity (stable 64-character hex output, distinguishes different inputs of the same length); step-file format checks (declares lane `core`, both write-locked paths, the four research sources `m_fixed.c` `tables.c` `d_main.c` `g_game.c`, prerequisite `00-018`).

- open_risks: The audit pins the marker pair contract entirely against the runtime `resolveMarkerRange` helper plus Chocolate Doom 2.2.1's `R_InitFlats`, `R_InitSpriteLumps`, `W_CheckNumForName`, and `W_GetNumForName` functions. A future runtime change that switches the marker resolution from a single forward scan to a per-name hash lookup (e.g., reusing `LumpLookup.checkNumForName` instead of walking the directory) would still satisfy the cross-check because both APIs preserve last-match-wins; however, if a future caller that needs to enumerate every duplicate of a marker name (vs. just resolving the pair) bypasses both APIs, the audit's `getAllIndicesForName` invariant from 05-003 would lapse silently for marker names. The audit deliberately treats inner sub-markers as ordinary content slots because that's what `R_InitFlats`/`R_InitSpriteLumps` do; the per-namespace catalog builders (`buildFlatCatalog`/`buildPatchCatalog`) carry the data-only count separately via the `isMarker` flag, and a future audit that pins the catalog-builder semantics will need to extend this audit's invariants rather than relax them. The audit pins the synthetic last-marker-wins case via `buildSyntheticDuplicateMarkerDirectory()` because the local `doom/DOOM1.WAD` is a single IWAD with no real duplicate marker pairs to exercise; a future step that loads a real PWAD (e.g. via `-file foo.wad`) which contributes its own `S_START`/`S_END` pair will need to extend the audit's runtime cross-check to verify that the IWAD+PWAD directory concatenation matches `W_AddFile`'s in-memory layout exactly and that the runtime `resolveMarkerRange` callers consume the assembled directory rather than per-WAD directories. The recurring parallel-lane working-tree race that fired during this cycle (the core lane's commit bc95cba and the launch lane's commit cc2283e prepended their HANDOFF_LOG.md entries while this lane was authoring its files) is still active for any future Ralph-loop step that touches `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md` or `plan_vanilla_parity/HANDOFF_LOG.md`; the recovery is documented in this entry's `recovery_edit` — re-apply the lane's plan-control edits on top of the merged file and re-run the canonical verification commands before staging. The parallel inventory lane's untracked WIP `test/vanilla_parity/current-state/inventory-core-math-and-timing-modules.test.ts` for the not-yet-committed 01-005 step carries a stale `claude_md_anchor` expectation `expect(status.claude_md_anchor).toContain('determinism')` that does not match the current CLAUDE.md text; these two failures surface in the full `bun test` suite but are entirely outside this lane's write lock and committed source, and will resolve when the inventory lane updates its WIP before its own commit. Lane lock `ef835e99-db26-4239-a914-5ec446213010` is held by the launcher and will be released on normal exit. ## 2026-04-26 - 03-005 implement-local-shareware-iwad-default-path

- status: completed

- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 local shareware IWAD default-path semantics layered on top of the broader IWAD discovery order pinned by 03-004. Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-local-shareware-iwad-default-path.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from any runtime IWAD discovery module (so a corrupted runtime cannot silently calibrate the audit's own probe table). The audit module exports `VanillaShareWareIwadDefaultPathContractAuditEntry` (one entry per behavioral axis) and `VANILLA_SHAREWARE_IWAD_DEFAULT_PATH_CONTRACT_AUDIT` (a frozen seven-entry ledger covering `SHAREWARE_BASENAME_IS_LOWERCASE_DOOM1_WAD_LITERAL` pinned to the verbatim `sprintf(name, "%s/doom1.wad", doomwaddir);` format string in the seventh access-block of `IdentifyVersion()`, `SHAREWARE_PATH_FORMAT_IS_DOOMWADDIR_PREFIXED_BASENAME` pinned to the `<doomwaddir>/doom1.wad` construction with the hard-coded forward-slash separator that vanilla never substitutes for a backslash even when the resolved doomwaddir contains backslashes, `SHAREWARE_DEFAULT_DIRECTORY_FALLS_BACK_TO_CURRENT_WORKING_DIRECTORY` pinned to the `if (!doomwaddir) doomwaddir = ".";` fallback yielding `./doom1.wad` and the present-but-empty edge-case yielding `/doom1.wad`, `SHAREWARE_GAMEMODE_IS_LITERAL_SHAREWARE_ENUM` pinned to the literal `gamemode = shareware;` assignment that fires unconditionally on access success without lump inspection, `SHAREWARE_PROBE_RUNS_LAST_AFTER_SIX_HIGHER_PRIORITY_CANDIDATES` pinned to the canonical six prior probes in order `doom2f.wad`, `doom2.wad`, `plutonia.wad`, `tnt.wad`, `doomu.wad`, `doom.wad`, `SHAREWARE_MISS_FALLS_THROUGH_TO_INDETERMINATE_PRINTOUT` pinned to the `printf("Game mode indeterminate.\n"); gamemode = indetermined;` fall-through with the noted Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 divergence (vanilla does not bail; CD 2.2.1 errors out), and `SHAREWARE_BASENAME_RESOLVES_CASE_INSENSITIVELY_ON_WINDOWS_ONLY` pinned to the lowercase literal vs uppercase on-disk casing distinction with the project's CLAUDE.md Windows-only constraint pinning the case-insensitive resolution path). ## 2026-04-26 - 04-004 audit-angle-type-and-wrap-semantics

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: core
- lock_id: 8e8565ef-3f37-4d3c-a83f-b7599f0d1e20
- step_id: 04-004
- step_title: audit-angle-type-and-wrap-semantics
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 angle_t type and wrap semantics implemented by `angleWrap` and the four `ANG*` constants in `src/core/angle.ts`. Wrote `src/core/audit-angle-type-and-wrap-semantics.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from `src/core/angle.ts` (so a corruption in angle.ts cannot silently corrupt the probe table that detects the corruption). The audit module exports six hand-pinned canonical constants (`AUDITED_ANG45 = 0x20000000`, `AUDITED_ANG90 = 0x40000000`, `AUDITED_ANG180 = 0x80000000`, `AUDITED_ANG270 = 0xC0000000`, `AUDITED_ANG_MAX = 0xFFFFFFFF`, `AUDITED_FULL_CIRCLE = 0x100000000`), a ten-entry `ANGLE_WRAP_AUDIT` ledger with stable identifier types covering six `c-source` facts (the `tables.h` typedef `typedef unsigned angle_t;`, plus the five named macro definitions for `ANG45`/`ANG90`/`ANG180`/`ANG270`/`ANG_MAX` with verbatim Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 spacing), three `wrap-rule` facts (the natural unsigned-arithmetic wrap rule that addition / subtraction inherit from the `unsigned` base type; the renderer FOV-delta site `anglea = ANG90 + (visangle-viewangle);` from `r_main.c` `R_ScaleFromGlobalAngle`; the player hitscan random-spread site `angle += (P_Random()-P_Random())<<18;` from `p_pspr.c` `P_GunShot`), and one `js-implementation` fact pinning the JS `>>> 0` ToUint32 operator decomposition that `angleWrap` uses. It exports a seven-entry `ANGLE_WRAP_INVARIANTS` ledger (WRAP_PRESERVES_VALUES_IN_UINT32_RANGE, WRAP_FULL_CIRCLE_RETURNS_ZERO, WRAP_NEGATIVE_ONE_RETURNS_ANG_MAX, WRAP_INT32_MIN_RETURNS_ANG180, WRAP_IS_IDEMPOTENT, WRAP_RESULT_IS_UINT32, WRAP_AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE), and a 25-entry curated `ANGLE_WRAP_PROBES` table covering seven categories (preserve, sum-wrap, negative-wrap, subtract-wrap, renderer-fov-delta, hitscan-random, demo-turn-carry) with hand-derived `expected` uint32 values for each. The hand-derived expectations include the parity-critical INT32_MIN→ANG180 reinterpretation, the renderer FOV-delta `ANG90 + (ANG45 - ANG270) → ANG225 (= 0xA0000000)` cross-quadrant case where both the inner subtract AND the outer add wrap, the player hitscan worst-case left spread `ANG90 + (-255 << 18) → 0x3C040000`, and the demo turn-carry edge case `0 - ANG_MAX → 1`. A BigInt reference function `angleWrapReference` models the canonical C unsigned wrap as `((BigInt(Math.trunc(input)) % 2^32n) + 2^32n) % 2^32n` (the mathematical-modulo formula required because BigInt's `%` operator preserves the sign of the dividend) for arbitrary-precision verification. The cross-check helper `crossCheckAngleWrapSemantics` accepts any candidate `(angle: number) => number` implementation and returns a `readonly string[]` of failure identifiers (`probe:<id>` / `invariant:<id>`); it returns an empty list for both the runtime `angleWrap` and the BigInt reference, and the focused test demonstrates six tampered-candidate failure modes (signed `| 0` instead of unsigned `>>> 0`; mask with `0x7FFFFFFF` dropping the high bit; `Math.abs` collapsing the negative-wrap; identity skipping the wrap entirely; subtract-2^32-once instead of taking modulo; float result that fails the int32-range invariant). Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-angle-type-and-wrap-semantics.test.ts` (56 tests, 377 expects) covering: audited canonical constants vs runtime exports vs hand-pinned hex literals; fact ledger shape (closed at exactly ten entries with the required category counts of 6 c-source + 3 wrap-rule + 1 js-implementation, every id unique, every description and cReference non-empty); fact ledger values (each c-source fact pins the verbatim canonical Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source line including spacing); invariant ledger shape (closed at exactly seven entries, every id unique); probe ledger shape (closed at exactly twenty-five entries, every id unique, every input finite, every expected value a uint32, every category covered); BigInt reference verification (every probe expected value matches the reference, the reference matches an independent BigInt formula on a sweep of representative integer inputs, the reference coerces non-finite inputs to zero, the reference truncates fractional inputs); runtime cross-check (the runtime `angleWrap` reports zero failures; reproduces every probe expected value; agrees with the BigInt reference for every probe; honours the canonical full-circle/negative-one/INT32_MIN/idempotent invariants; reproduces the canonical R_ScaleFromGlobalAngle FOV-delta and P_GunShot worst-case-left-spread results); failure-mode tests (six tampered candidates each detected by their expected probe / invariant identifiers); step-file format checks (the step declares lane `core`, both write-locked paths, the four research sources `m_fixed.c` `tables.c` `d_main.c` `g_game.c`, and prerequisite `00-018`). Marked 04-004 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md` and ticked the step-file `[ ]` to `[x]`.

for (i = startlump; i < numlumps_total; ++i) { lumpinfo_t *lump_p = &filelumps[i - startlump]; ... strncpy(lump_p->name, filerover->name, 8); lumpinfo[i] = lump_p; ++filerover; }` body that establishes append-only load order, intra-wad duplicate preservation, and directory-order-within-wad preservation); upstream `src/w_wad.c` `W_CheckNumForName` (the `// scan backwards so patch lump files take precedence` linear-fallback path `for (i = numlumps_total - 1; i >= 0; --i) { if (!strncasecmp(lumpinfo[i]->name, name, 8)) return i; The audit also assumes `getAllIndicesForName` is the single canonical enumeration API for callers that need to see every duplicate; if a future caller bypasses it (e.g. by directly indexing `liveDirectory[i]` and filtering by name), the audit's assertion that "callers MUST use this enumeration" becomes only advisory. - summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 startup error path and `I_Error` cleanup-fan-out semantics to their Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 reference (`src/i_system.c` `I_Error`, `I_Quit`, `I_AtExit` plus the call sites in `src/d_main.c`, `src/g_game.c`, `src/i_video.c`, `src/m_menu.c`) and cross-checked the runtime `QuitFlow` class in `src/bootstrap/quitFlow.ts` against that contract. Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-startup-error-path-and-i-error-semantics.ts` as the audit module, exporting (a) `VANILLA_I_ERROR_CONTRACT_AUDIT` — five clauses pinning I_Error's `already_quitting` recursive-call sentinel, the `run_on_error` filter that gates dispatch on the error path, the head-to-tail traversal of `exit_funcs` that yields LIFO execution because I_AtExit prepends, the stderr `"\nError: "` prefix and `"\n\n"` suffix bracketing the vfprintf body, and the non-zero process exit; (b) `VANILLA_I_QUIT_CONTRACT_AUDIT` — three clauses pinning the unconditional dispatch of every entry regardless of `run_on_error`, the same head-to-tail LIFO traversal, and the zero process exit; (c) `VANILLA_I_ATEXIT_CONTRACT_AUDIT` — two clauses pinning the linked-list head-prepend (`entry->next = exit_funcs; exit_funcs = entry;`) and the verbatim preservation of the caller-supplied `run_on_error` flag; (d) `VANILLA_STARTUP_ERROR_PATH_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` — seven high-level invariants the cross-check enforces (`ERROR_PATH_RUNS_ONLY_RUN_ON_ERROR_HANDLERS`, `NORMAL_PATH_RUNS_ALL_HANDLERS`, `BOTH_PATHS_USE_LIFO_ORDER`, `SHAREWARE_CANONICAL_PATHS_ARE_IDENTICAL`, `RECURSIVE_QUIT_IS_REJECTED`, `REGISTER_AFTER_QUIT_IS_REJECTED`, `EMPTY_REGISTRATION_RUNS_NO_HANDLERS`); (e) `VANILLA_STARTUP_ERROR_PATH_PROBES` — eleven concrete `(registrations, dispatchKind, recursiveFollowUp) → (expectedExecution, expectsRecursiveRejection)` probes covering every derived invariant including the empty-registration zero-execution case for both error and normal paths, the `runOnError: false` filter case for both paths, the three-handler LIFO-order case for both paths, the canonical 8-handler shareware case where I_Error and I_Quit produce CANONICAL_QUIT_ORDER verbatim because every shareware handler has `runOnError == true`, the recursive `executeErrorQuit` and `executeQuit` rejection cases (modeling the `already_quitting` sentinel via the runtime `#hasQuit` guard that throws), and the post-quit `register` rejection case; (f) `VanillaStartupErrorPathHandler` handler-shape interface, `REFERENCE_VANILLA_STARTUP_ERROR_PATH_HANDLER` adapter that routes every probe to a fresh `QuitFlow` instance, `VANILLA_SHAREWARE_CANONICAL_HANDLER_COUNT` mirror of `CLEANUP_STEP_COUNT` (8), `deriveExpectedDispatchSequence` helper that computes the expected LIFO sequence independently of `QuitFlow` (used by the focused test to cross-validate every probe's `expectedExecution` against the contract), and `crossCheckVanillaStartupErrorPath` cross-check helper that applies every probe and reports failures by stable identifier (`probe:<id>:execution:length-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:execution:order-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:recursive:expected-rejection-missing`, `probe:<id>:recursive:unexpected-rejection`, `probe:<id>:recursive:expected-followup-skipped`). Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-startup-error-path-and-i-error-semantics.test.ts` (42 tests, 154 expects) that asserts the audit ledger shapes (every clause id is unique, every clause references `src/i_system.c`, every clause carries a non-empty invariant, every probe witnesses an existing derived invariant, every derived invariant is witnessed by at least one probe, every probe's `expectedExecution` matches `deriveExpectedDispatchSequence` when fed the same registrations and dispatchKind), asserts `crossCheckVanillaStartupErrorPath(REFERENCE_VANILLA_STARTUP_ERROR_PATH_HANDLER)` returns zero failures (the runtime `QuitFlow` class satisfies every probe), proves five failure modes with synthetic broken adapters (a handler that drops the `runOnError` filter on the error path fails the `error-path-skips-run-on-error-false` probe, a handler that uses FIFO order fails both `lifo-order-three-handlers-error-path` and `lifo-order-three-handlers-normal-path`, a handler that does not reject a second dispatch fails the recursive-rejection probes, a handler that runs zero handlers fails both LIFO-order and shareware-canonical length checks, and a handler that returns a recursive-rejection flag for a no-followup probe fails the `unexpected-rejection` check), exercises the runtime `QuitFlow` class directly with five targeted assertions (canonical shareware `executeErrorQuit` matches CANONICAL_QUIT_ORDER, canonical shareware `executeQuit` matches CANONICAL_QUIT_ORDER, a handler with `runOnError == false` is skipped on the error path but runs on the normal path, a second `executeErrorQuit` after the first throws, a second `executeQuit` after the first throws, registering after `executeErrorQuit` throws), exercises `deriveExpectedDispatchSequence` directly with three targeted assertions (mixed-flag normal path returns full LIFO, mixed-flag error path returns filtered LIFO, empty registration list returns empty for both paths), and asserts the step file 03-003 declares the launch lane, the implement write lock, the five canonical research sources (`d_main.c`, `g_game.c`, `i_timer.c`, `i_video.c`, `m_menu.c`), and the prerequisite gate `00-018`. Marked 03-003 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.

## 2026-04-26 - 03-002 implement-vanilla-command-line-parsing

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: launch
- lock_id: cdec5b6e-5605-4278-a008-7162c41bad09
- step_id: 03-002
- step_title: implement-vanilla-command-line-parsing
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 command-line parsing contract to its Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 reference (`src/m_argv.c` `M_CheckParm` and `M_CheckParmWithArgs`, plus the single-dash flag convention used throughout `src/d_main.c`) and cross-checked the runtime `CommandLine` class in `src/bootstrap/cmdline.ts` against that contract. Wrote `src/bootstrap/implement-vanilla-command-line-parsing.ts` as the audit module, exporting (a) `VANILLA_M_CHECKPARM_CONTRACT_AUDIT` — five contract clauses pinning M_CheckParm's not-found sentinel zero, 1-based found-index, case-insensitive equality (strcasecmp), index-1 scan start (program-name skip), and exact-string equality (no substring match); (b) `VANILLA_M_CHECKPARM_WITH_ARGS_CONTRACT_AUDIT` — three contract clauses pinning the not-found sentinel zero, the trailing-args minimum (`index + requiredArgs < myargc`), and the same 1-based index return when arity holds; (c) `VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_DASH_CONVENTION_AUDIT` — two conventions pinning the single-dash flag prefix and the value-immediately-after-flag slot rule; (d) `VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` — six high-level invariants the cross-check enforces (`CHECKPARM_ZERO_IS_NOT_FOUND_SENTINEL`, `CHECKPARM_IS_CASE_INSENSITIVE`, `CHECKPARM_NEVER_MATCHES_PROGRAM_NAME`, `CHECKPARM_REQUIRES_EXACT_STRING_EQUALITY`, `CHECKPARM_WITH_ARGS_GUARDS_VALUE_READS`, `VANILLA_FLAGS_USE_SINGLE_DASH_PREFIX`); (e) `VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_PROBES` — ten concrete `(argv, probedName) → (expectedCheckParm, expectedExists, expectedTrailingArgs, expectedGetParameter)` probes covering every derived invariant including the program-name-on-its-own (argv `["-iwad"]` → 0) and program-name-shadowed-by-real-flag (argv `["-iwad", "-iwad", "DOOM1.WAD"]` → 1) edge cases, the `-warp` two-trailing-arg case, and the `-iwadextra` substring-rejection case; (f) `VanillaCommandLineParser` parser-shape interface, `REFERENCE_VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_PARSER` adapter that routes every method to a fresh `CommandLine` instance, and `crossCheckVanillaCommandLineParser` cross-check helper that applies every probe and reports failures by stable identifier (`probe:<id>:checkParameter:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:parameterExists:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:checkParameterWithArgs:value-mismatch`, `probe:<id>:getParameter:value-mismatch`). Added focused test `test/vanilla_parity/launch/implement-vanilla-command-line-parsing.test.ts` (39 tests, 137 expects) that asserts the audit ledger shapes (every clause id is unique, every clause references `src/m_argv.c`/`src/d_main.c`, every clause carries a non-empty invariant, every probe witnesses an existing derived invariant, every derived invariant is witnessed by at least one probe, every found-index probe targets a valid argv slot), asserts `crossCheckVanillaCommandLineParser(REFERENCE_VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_PARSER)` returns zero failures (the runtime `CommandLine` class satisfies every probe), proves five failure modes with synthetic broken adapters (a case-sensitive parser fails the case-insensitive probes, a substring-matching parser fails the exact-match probe, a parser scanning from index 0 fails the program-name-skip probe, a parser ignoring the trailing-args minimum fails the with-args-rejects-tail-flag probe, and a parser returning 0-based indices fails the found-returns-one-based-index probe), exercises the runtime `CommandLine` directly with nine targeted `(argv, probe) → result` assertions, and asserts the step file 03-002 declares the launch lane, the implement write lock, the five canonical research sources (`d_main.c`, `g_game.c`, `i_timer.c`, `i_video.c`, `m_menu.c`), and the prerequisite gate `00-018`. Marked 03-002 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.

- recovery_edit: One in-place edit. The first typecheck pass surfaced TS7006 implicit-any errors on the four arrow-function parameters of `REFERENCE_VANILLA_COMMANDLINE_PARSER` because TypeScript's contextual-type inference does not flow through `Object.freeze({...})` to the inner method literals. Added explicit parameter types (`argv: readonly string[]`, `name: string`, `requiredArgs: number`) and explicit return types on each routed method literal, re-ran the typecheck, full suite, and focused test — all clean. No other recovery edits were needed; one local data fix during initial drafting corrected the program-name-shadowed-by-real-flag probe's expected `getParameter` value from the wrong `-iwad` to the correct `DOOM1.WAD` (the value after argv[1], not argv[0], because `getParameter` reads `argv[index+1]` where `index === 1`).

only paths/sizes/hashes/derived metadata of files inside the read-only reference roots `doom/`, `iwad/`, `reference/` are allowed), the canonical inventory step file contract (every `plan_vanilla_parity/steps/01-NNN-<slug>.md` declares `lane: inventory`, lists exactly two write-locked paths `plan_vanilla_parity/current-state/<slug>.json` and `test/vanilla_parity/current-state/<slug>.test.ts` under both `## write lock` and `## expected changes`, and satisfies the canonical fourteen-field shape pinned by `plan_vanilla_parity/define-step-file-required-fields.md`), the canonical inventory test contract (every `test/vanilla_parity/current-state/<slug>.test.ts` loads the artifact via `Bun.file().json()`, asserts every canonical required field is present and well-typed, asserts every `follow_up_steps` entry resolves to an existing step file, and includes at least one failure-mode test), the canonical seventeen evidence locations (the example inventory artifact, the example inventory step file, the example inventory test file, every adjacent governance pin, the `inventory` row source `plan_vanilla_parity/PARALLEL_WORK.md`, the policy module `src/reference/policy.ts`, AGENTS.md, CLAUDE.md, the four plan_vanilla_parity governance index files), and the canonical acceptance phrasing that names the canonical artifact directory, every required field in backticks, the literal `inventory` lane, every read-only root, and the focused-test contract path. - summary: Pinned the Bun-exclusive runtime and package command rule that every Ralph-loop step must follow when invoking, installing, building, testing, or executing scripts in this repository. Wrote `plan_vanilla_parity/ban-non-bun-runtime-and-package-commands.md` as a parseable governance document with sixteen required sections: `scope name` (`vanilla DOOM 1.9 Bun runtime and package command exclusivity`), `emulated vanilla version` (`1.9`), `reference engine` (`Chocolate Doom`), `reference engine version` (`2.2.1`), `bun exclusivity rule` (anchors AGENTS.md "This project uses Bun. Always." Runtime declaration and CLAUDE.md "Bun only." Runtime constraints declaration, names every forbidden command in backticks, forbids "if Bun is installed" fallbacks and Node.js compatibility paths), `sanctioned bun commands` (the eight canonical Bun command surfaces `bun`, `bun add`, `bun build`, `bun install`, `bun remove`, `bun run`, `bun test`, `bun x` ASCIIbetically sorted), `forbidden runtime commands` (`node`, `ts-node`, `tsx`), `forbidden package manager commands` (`npm`, `npx`, `pnpm`, `yarn`), `forbidden test runner commands` (`jest`, `mocha`, `vitest`), `forbidden command list` (the union of all three forbidden categories: `jest`, `mocha`, `node`, `npm`, `npx`, `pnpm`, `ts-node`, `tsx`, `vitest`, `yarn` — exactly the ten entries in `BANNED_COMMANDS` of `plan_vanilla_parity/validate-plan.ts`), `forbidden lockfiles` (`package-lock.json`, `pnpm-lock.yaml`, `yarn.lock`), `sanctioned lockfile` (`bun.lock`), `bun native api preference` (anchors the ten Bun-native APIs `Bun.argv`, `Bun.env`, `Bun.file`, `Bun.serve`, `Bun.sleep`, `Bun.spawn`, `Bun.write`, `bun:ffi`, `bun:sqlite`, `bun:test` and the five `@bun-win32/*` Win32 binding packages `@bun-win32/core`, `@bun-win32/gdi32`, `@bun-win32/kernel32`, `@bun-win32/user32`, `@bun-win32/winmm`), `verification command rule` (anchors the four canonical verification commands `bun run format`, `bun test <path>`, `bun test`, `bun x tsc --noEmit --project tsconfig.json` and pins that `validate-plan.ts` `BANNED_COMMANDS` enforces this against every step file's `verification commands` section), `evidence locations` (AGENTS.md, CLAUDE.md, package.json, plan_vanilla_parity MASTER_CHECKLIST/PROMPT/README, validate-plan.ts), and `acceptance phrasing` (the canonical `Bun is the only sanctioned runtime, package manager, script runner, and test runner; never ...` line that lists every forbidden command in backticks). Always." declaration, the bun.lock lockfile pin, every forbidden command and Bun-native API in backticks), anchors the CLAUDE.md Runtime constraints section (the "**Bun only.**" declaration, every forbidden command in backticks), anchors the plan_vanilla_parity README.md Ralph-loop rules line that forbids the same ten non-Bun commands, parses `package.json` and proves every committed script starts with `bun ` and never invokes any forbidden command, anchors the step file `plan_vanilla_parity/steps/00-007-ban-non-bun-runtime-and-package-commands.md` (governance lane, write-locked declaration document, write-locked focused test), locks the MASTER_CHECKLIST.md row with both pending `[ ]` and completed `[x]` row variants, locks the canonical acceptance phrasing, asserts every evidence location exists on disk and is a file, asserts every list is ASCIIbetically sorted with no duplicates, asserts the sanctioned bun commands and the forbidden command list are disjoint sets (with a per-token check for the `bun add`/`bun build`/etc. multi-token entries), and asserts the union of forbidden runtime + package manager + test runner equals the comprehensive forbidden command list. ## 2026-04-26 - 04-001 audit-fixed-point-constants

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7

- lock_id: 25e4d10c-91ff-4a27-bc1f-d51dd016d3d3
