- step_title: audit-fixed-point-constants
- summary: Pinned the four fixed-point constants exported by `src/core/fixed.ts` (`FRACBITS`, `FRACUNIT`, `FIXED_MAX`, `FIXED_MIN`) to their upstream Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 declarations and the int32 backing type that vanilla 16.16 fixed-point depends on. Wrote `src/core/audit-fixed-point-constants.ts` as the audit ledger module exporting `FixedPointConstantAuditEntry` (one entry per constant pinning name, value, hex literal, underlyingBitWidth=32, the verbatim C declaration `#define FRACBITS 16` / `#define FRACUNIT (1<<FRACBITS)` and the derived `INT_MAX`/`INT_MIN` clamps used by `FixedDiv`, the source file `src/m_fixed.h` or `derived`, and a plain-language invariant), `FIXED_POINT_CONSTANT_AUDIT` (frozen four-entry array), `FixedPointDerivedInvariant`/`FIXED_POINT_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` (eleven invariants enumerated by stable identifier — `FRACUNIT_EQUALS_ONE_SHIFTED_BY_FRACBITS`, `FRACUNIT_IS_POWER_OF_TWO`, `FIXED_MAX_IS_INT32_MAX`, `FIXED_MIN_IS_INT32_MIN`, `FIXED_RANGE_SPANS_2_TO_32`, `FIXED_MAX_INTEGER_PART_IS_INT16_MAX`, `FIXED_MIN_INTEGER_PART_IS_INT16_MIN`, `FIXED_MAX_FRACTIONAL_PART_IS_SATURATED`, `FIXED_MIN_FRACTIONAL_PART_IS_ZERO`, `INT32_WRAP_AROUND_FROM_MAX_TO_MIN`, `INT32_WRAP_AROUND_FROM_MIN_TO_MAX`), `FixedPointConstantSnapshot`, and `crossCheckFixedPointConstants(snapshot)` which returns the failure list (`audit:<NAME>:value-mismatch` for value mismatches and `derived:<INVARIANT_ID>` for derived-invariant failures). Wrote the focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-fixed-point-constants.test.ts` (34 tests, 103 expects) that locks the ledger shape (audits exactly four constants, every name unique, every name maps to a runtime export of `src/core/fixed.ts`, every entry pins `underlyingBitWidth = 32`, every entry references an allowed Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 source file `src/m_fixed.h` / `src/doomtype.h` / `derived`, every entry carries a non-empty C declaration and invariant), the per-constant ledger values (`FRACBITS = 16`, `0x10`, `#define FRACBITS 16`; `FRACUNIT = 65_536`, `0x10000`, `#define FRACUNIT (1<<FRACBITS)`; `FIXED_MAX = 0x7FFF_FFFF`, hex literal `0x7FFFFFFF`; `FIXED_MIN = -0x8000_0000`, hex literal `-0x80000000`), the hex round-trip via `Number.parseInt`, the eleven derived invariants by stable id with non-empty descriptions, the cross-check on the live runtime snapshot returning zero failures along with seven runtime invariants (`FRACUNIT === 1 << FRACBITS`, `FIXED_MAX >> FRACBITS === 32_767`, `FIXED_MIN >> FRACBITS === -32_768`, `FIXED_MAX & (FRACUNIT - 1) === 0xFFFF`, `FIXED_MIN & (FRACUNIT - 1) === 0`, `(FIXED_MAX + 1) | 0 === FIXED_MIN`, `(FIXED_MIN - 1) | 0 === FIXED_MAX`, `FIXED_MAX - FIXED_MIN + 1 === 2 ** 32`), and seven failure-mode tests proving the cross-check detects a tampered FRACBITS that breaks the 16.16 split (returns `audit:FRACBITS:value-mismatch`, `derived:FRACUNIT_EQUALS_ONE_SHIFTED_BY_FRACBITS`, `derived:FIXED_MAX_INTEGER_PART_IS_INT16_MAX`, `derived:FIXED_MIN_INTEGER_PART_IS_INT16_MIN`), a tampered FRACUNIT that no longer equals `1 << FRACBITS`, a non-power-of-two FRACUNIT, a clamped FIXED_MAX, a tampered FIXED_MIN, a fractional-saturation regression on FIXED_MAX, and an integer-aligned regression on FIXED_MIN; plus two step-file tests that lock the `## lane\\n\\ncore` declaration, the audit/test paths under the write lock, and the four research sources `m_fixed.c`, `tables.c`, `d_main.c`, and `g_game.c`. Marked 04-001 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.

- summary: Pinned the byte-level layout of the vanilla DOOM 1.9 WAD file header (`wadinfo_t`, 12 bytes) and directory entry (`filelump_t`, 16 bytes) parsed by `src/wad/header.ts` and `src/wad/directory.ts` to their upstream Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 declarations in `src/w_wad.h` / `src/w_wad.c`. Wrote `src/assets/verify-wad-header-and-directory-parsing.ts` as the audit ledger module exporting `WadStructFieldAuditEntry` (one entry per byte-level field — `identification` (offset 0, char[4], 4 bytes), `numlumps` (offset 4, int LE, 4 bytes), `infotableofs` (offset 8, int LE, 4 bytes) for `wadinfo_t`; `filepos` (offset 0, int LE, 4 bytes), `size` (offset 4, int LE, 4 bytes), `name` (offset 8, char[8], 8 bytes) for `filelump_t`), `WAD_STRUCT_FIELD_AUDIT` (frozen six-entry array), `WadStructSizeAuditEntry`/`WAD_STRUCT_SIZE_AUDIT` (pinning `WAD_HEADER_SIZE === 12` and `DIRECTORY_ENTRY_SIZE === 16` to their `PACKEDATTR` struct totals), `WadIdentificationAuditEntry`/`WAD_IDENTIFICATION_AUDIT` (the two valid identification tags `IWAD` and `PWAD` declared by `W_AddFile`), `WadStructDerivedInvariant`/`WAD_STRUCT_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` (seven derived invariants — `WADINFO_FIELD_OFFSETS_ARE_CONTIGUOUS`, `WADINFO_TOTAL_BYTE_SIZE_EQUALS_TWELVE`, `FILELUMP_FIELD_OFFSETS_ARE_CONTIGUOUS`, `FILELUMP_TOTAL_BYTE_SIZE_EQUALS_SIXTEEN`, `IDENTIFICATION_VALID_TAGS_ARE_IWAD_AND_PWAD`, `INTEGER_FIELDS_ARE_LITTLE_ENDIAN`, `NAME_FIELD_IS_EIGHT_BYTE_ASCII`), `WadStructLayoutSnapshot`, `crossCheckWadStructLayout(snapshot)` (returns failure list of `audit:size:<NAME>:value-mismatch`, `audit:identifications:<TAG>:missing`, `audit:identifications:unexpected:<TAG>`, `derived:<INVARIANT_ID>` identifiers), `ShareWareDoom1WadOracle`/`SHAREWARE_DOOM1_WAD_ORACLE` (pinned facts about the local shareware `doom/DOOM1.WAD` — fileSize 4_196_020, identification `IWAD`, lumpCount 1264, directoryOffset 4_175_796, directoryEnd 4_196_020, firstLumpName `PLAYPAL`, lastLumpName `F_END`, firstLumpFilePos 12, firstLumpSize 10_752 = 14 palettes * 768 bytes), `ShareWareDoom1WadSample`, and `crossCheckShareWareDoom1WadSample(sample)` (returns failure list of `oracle:<field>:value-mismatch` identifiers). Wrote the focused test `test/vanilla_parity/wad/verify-wad-header-and-directory-parsing.test.ts` (49 tests, 146 expects) that locks the field-audit ledger shape (exactly six fields split three-and-three between `wadinfo_t` and `filelump_t`, every (struct, fieldName) pair unique, every name in the allowed enumeration, every reference source `src/w_wad.h`, every C declaration and invariant non-empty, char fields carry `endianness === 'n/a'` and int fields carry `endianness === 'little'`), the per-field byte offsets and widths, the size audit ledger (two entries pinning `WAD_HEADER_SIZE === 12` and `DIRECTORY_ENTRY_SIZE === 16`), the identification audit ledger (exactly the two tags `IWAD` and `PWAD`, both referencing `src/w_wad.c`), the seven derived invariants by stable id with non-empty descriptions, the cross-check on the live runtime snapshot returning zero failures along with two contiguity invariants summing to 12 and 16 bytes, five failure-mode tests proving the cross-check detects a tampered `WAD_HEADER_SIZE`, a tampered `DIRECTORY_ENTRY_SIZE`, a missing `IWAD` tag, an unexpected third tag `XWAD`, and reports a clean failure list for an equivalent fresh snapshot, the live shareware DOOM1.WAD oracle (file size, identification, lump count, directoryOffset, directoryEnd matching wadBuffer.length, PLAYPAL first / F_END last, PLAYPAL is exactly 14 * 768 = 10752 bytes at file offset 12, lump count cross-checks against `PRIMARY_TARGET.wadLumpCount`, filename cross-checks against `PRIMARY_TARGET.wadFilename`, sample cross-check returns zero failures, lump count and wadType cross-check against `reference/manifests/wad-map-summary.json`), and seven failure-mode tests proving the oracle cross-check detects a wrong file size, a PWAD identification on an IWAD, a tampered lump count (which also surfaces a `directoryEnd` mismatch), a wrong first lump name, a wrong last lump name, a wrong PLAYPAL file position, and a wrong PLAYPAL size; never batch multiple steps into one push at session end; an unpushed commit is at-risk work; if `git push` fails the agent must report the blocker and not declare the loop successful), `push failure rule` (forbids marking the row `[x]` in MASTER_CHECKLIST.md, writing `status: completed` to HANDOFF_LOG.md, or returning `RLP_STATUS: COMPLETED` when `git push` fails; - files_changed: D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/plan_vanilla_parity/pin-local-git-direct-commit-and-push-workflow.md; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/test/plan_vanilla_parity/pin-local-git-direct-commit-and-push-workflow.test.ts; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/plan_vanilla_parity/HANDOFF_LOG.md
- recovery_edit: First focused-test run flagged two ASCIIbetical sort assertions that disagreed with JS default `Array.prototype.sort` collation: (1) the `forbidden commit attribution markers` list put `🤖` (U+1F916, surrogate pair high `0xD83E`) first, but `.sort()` puts the surrogate-pair string after every ASCII string, so the document and the `CANONICAL_FORBIDDEN_ATTRIBUTION_MARKERS` constant were both reordered to put `🤖` last; (2) the `forbidden git stage commands` list put `git add -A` before `git add --all`, but at byte offset 8 both share `-` and at offset 9 the `.sort()` collation makes `-` (45) less than `A` (65), so `--all` correctly precedes `-A`. Reordered the document bullets to `git add --all`, `git add -A`, `git add .`, `git commit --all`, `git commit -a`, updated the `CANONICAL_FORBIDDEN_STAGE_COMMANDS` constant to match, and updated the failure-mode regex in `parser surfaces a meaningful error when forbidden git stage commands is empty` to match the new bullet ordering. After both fixes the focused test passes 32/32, the full suite passes 8246/8246, typecheck is clean, and plan validation reports 398 steps with first step 00-001.

Not found.` / `return -1;`; `get-throws-on-miss` pinned to `i = W_CheckNumForName (name);` / `if (i == -1)` / `I_Error ("W_GetNumForName: %s not found!", name);`), `LUMP_LOOKUP_SEMANTIC_AUDIT` (frozen five-entry array), `LumpLookupDerivedInvariant` / `LUMP_LOOKUP_DERIVED_INVARIANTS` (seven derived invariants — `CHECK_NUM_FOR_NAME_IS_CASE_INSENSITIVE`, `CHECK_NUM_FOR_NAME_LAST_MATCH_WINS`, `CHECK_NUM_FOR_NAME_RETURNS_NEGATIVE_ONE_ON_MISS`, `GET_NUM_FOR_NAME_THROWS_ON_MISS`, `CHECK_AND_GET_AGREE_ON_HITS`, `UNIQUE_COUNT_NEVER_EXCEEDS_TOTAL_COUNT`, `EIGHT_BYTE_NAME_FIELD`), `LumpLookupSnapshot` (runtime-behavior shape with `checkPlaypalUpper` / `checkPlaypalLower` / `checkPlaypalMixed` / `checkMiss` / `getPlaypal` / `getMissThrows` / `lastMatchWinsResult` / `totalCount` / `uniqueCount`), `crossCheckLumpLookupSemantics(snapshot)` (returns failure list of `derived:<INVARIANT_ID>` and `audit:<AXIS_ID>:not-observed` identifiers), `ShareWareDoom1WadLookupOracle` / `SHAREWARE_DOOM1_WAD_LOOKUP_ORACLE` (pinned facts about the local shareware `doom/DOOM1.WAD` lookup — totalCount 1264, playpalIndex 0, colormapIndex 1, hasE1M1 true, hasTexture1 true, hasTexture2 false (registered/Ultimate-only), hasDemo1 true, hasFEnd true), `ShareWareDoom1WadLookupSample`, and `crossCheckShareWareDoom1WadLookupSample(sample)` (returns failure list of `oracle:<field>:value-mismatch` identifiers). The TS runtime does NOT truncate names beyond 8 chars (`Map.get(name.toUpperCase())` keys on the full string) whereas vanilla `strncpy(name8, name, 8)` truncates to 8 bytes; this divergence only manifests if a caller passes a 9+ char name AND the directory contains an 8-char-truncation match, which neither shareware DOOM1.WAD nor any registered/Ultimate IWAD does at any active callsite. If a future PWAD or call path begins passing > 8 char names, an oracle-capture follow-up step must extend the audit ledger to enforce truncation parity. ## 2026-04-26 - 04-002 audit-fixed-multiply-overflow-semantics

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: core
- lock_id: 8e8565ef-3f37-4d3c-a83f-b7599f0d1e20
- step_id: 04-002
- step_title: audit-fixed-multiply-overflow-semantics
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 fixed-point multiply overflow semantics implemented by `fixedMul` in `src/core/fixed.ts`. Wrote `src/core/audit-fixed-multiply-overflow-semantics.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from `src/core/fixed.ts` (so a corruption in fixed.ts cannot silently corrupt the probe table that detects the corruption). The audit module exports four hand-pinned canonical constants (`AUDITED_FRACBITS = 16`, `AUDITED_FRACUNIT = 65_536`, `AUDITED_FIXED_MAX = 0x7FFFFFFF`, `AUDITED_FIXED_MIN = -0x80000000`), a ten-entry `FIXED_MUL_OVERFLOW_AUDIT` ledger with stable identifier types covering four `c-source` facts (the `m_fixed.h` header signature `fixed_t FixedMul(fixed_t a, fixed_t b);`, the int64 promotion in the body `return ((int64_t) a * (int64_t) b) >> FRACBITS;`, the arithmetic-right-shift rule on signed int64, and the implicit narrowing cast back to `fixed_t` on return), five `overflow-rule` facts (modulo-2^32 wrap, arithmetic-right-shift rounds toward -inf, identity-by-FRACUNIT, zero-absorbs, commutativity), and one `js-implementation` fact pinning the four-partial-product 16x16 decomposition in `src/core/fixed.ts` as bounded by 2^46 (well below `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER`). It exports a seven-entry `FIXED_MUL_OVERFLOW_INVARIANTS` ledger (IDENTITY_BY_FRACUNIT_LEFT, IDENTITY_BY_FRACUNIT_RIGHT, ZERO_LEFT_ABSORBS, ZERO_RIGHT_ABSORBS, COMMUTATIVE, INT32_RANGE_RESULT, AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE), and a 25-entry curated `FIXED_MUL_OVERFLOW_PROBES` table covering eight categories (identity, zero, integer, fractional, wrap, rounding, sub-unit, extreme) with hand-derived `expected` values for each. The hand-derived expectations include the four documented wraps (FIXED_MAX^2 = -FRACUNIT, FIXED_MIN^2 = 0, FIXED_MIN*FRACUNIT = FIXED_MIN, FIXED_MAX*FRACUNIT = FIXED_MAX), the cross-extreme `FIXED_MAX * FIXED_MIN = 32768` derived through int48 to int32 wrap, the rounding-toward-negative-infinity examples (`-3 * 1 = -1`, `-1 * 1 = -1`), the (-1)*(-1)=0 case where the multiplication flips sign before the shift, the `wrap_FIXED_MAX_x_two = -2` and `wrap_FIXED_MIN_x_two = 0` cases (the latter exact-multiple-of-2^32 wrap), and the sub-unit carry preservation `(FRACUNIT+1)^2 = FRACUNIT+2`. It exports a `fixedMulReference(a, b)` BigInt-based reference implementation modelling the canonical C body `Number(BigInt.asIntN(32, (BigInt(a) * BigInt(b)) >> 16n))` bit-for-bit and a `crossCheckFixedMulOverflowSemantics(fixedMulFn)` helper that returns failure ids `probe:<id>` for any per-probe expectation mismatch and `invariant:<id>` for any derived-invariant violation across the full probe-input sweep. Wrote the focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-fixed-multiply-overflow-semantics.test.ts` (42 tests, 560 expects) that asserts the audited canonical constants agree with the runtime exports from `src/core/fixed.ts`, locks the ledger shape (exactly 10 facts split 4/5/1 across categories, 7 invariants, 25 probes covering 8 categories), pins specific fact values (the verbatim C signature and body strings, the int32-only operand/expected typing for every probe), verifies the BigInt reference agrees with every probe expectation AND with an inline `Number(BigInt.asIntN(32, ...))` independent reference on a 17x17 sweep of representative int32 values (289 cross-checks), runs `crossCheckFixedMulOverflowSemantics(fixedMul)` against the live runtime and asserts zero failures, asserts the runtime honours every documented invariant on the canonical wrap examples (`fixedMul(FIXED_MAX, FIXED_MAX) === -FRACUNIT`, `fixedMul(FIXED_MIN, FIXED_MIN) === 0`, the three rounding-toward-neg-inf cases, the two extreme identity preservations), and proves five distinct failure-mode tampering candidates are detected (a `Math.imul`-based candidate that drops the high bits of the product before the shift fails `probe:identity_FRACUNIT_x_FRACUNIT` and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; a BigInt-division candidate that truncates toward zero instead of toward -inf fails `probe:rounding_neg_three_x_one`, `probe:rounding_neg_one_x_one`, and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; a saturating candidate that clamps to FIXED_MAX/FIXED_MIN instead of wrapping fails `probe:wrap_FIXED_MAX_squared`, `probe:wrap_FIXED_MAX_x_two`, and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; a no-narrowing candidate that returns the raw shifted BigInt as a Number fails `probe:wrap_FIXED_MAX_squared` and `invariant:INT32_RANGE_RESULT`; a deliberately asymmetric candidate fails `invariant:COMMUTATIVE`; the BigInt reference itself reports zero failures). Three step-file tests lock the `## lane: core` declaration, the `## write lock` paths, the `## research sources` listing of `m_fixed.c` / `tables.c` / `d_main.c` / `g_game.c`, and the `## prerequisites: 00-018` declaration. Marked 04-002 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.

The local `Set` instances are still functionally read-only — they are constructed from frozen literal arrays and never mutated by the test — but the type annotation now matches the `.toEqual` overload that Bun matchers expose. One audit test does cross-check the audited canonical values against the runtime exports — that test catches drift between the two sources of truth, but if BOTH are corrupted in the same direction in the same commit, the drift goes undetected. Mitigation: the focused test BigInt reference (`Number(BigInt.asIntN(32, (BigInt(a) * BigInt(b)) >> 16n))`) is recomputed inline from constants `16n`, not from the audited constants, so any drift in `AUDITED_FRACBITS` would surface as a probe expectation mismatch. The audit-vs-runtime cross-check is also enforced by the existing 04-001 `audit-fixed-point-constants.ts` ledger, so a tampered fixed.ts that survived this audit would fail the constants audit independently. - open_risks: The audit pins vanilla DOOM 1.9 `IdentifyVersion()` discovery order, which differs from Chocolate Doom 2.2.1's `D_FindIWAD`/`BuildIWADDirList` multi-directory search. A future Ralph-loop step that implements the runtime IWAD discovery for this project must choose: (a) implement the vanilla single-directory order this audit pins (matching the audit's seven candidates and verbatim probe order), or (b) extend the audit to add a Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 contract layer that pins the multi-directory and `-iwad` extensions. The audit deliberately stops at vanilla because the project's primary target (`plan_vanilla_parity/SOURCE_CATALOG.md` authority 1) is the local DOS binary `doom/DOOMD.EXE`, which has no `-iwad` flag and no multi-directory search. The candidate list intentionally includes `doom2f.wad`/`doom2.wad`/`plutonia.wad`/`tnt.wad` even though the project's scope is shareware/registered/Ultimate only — pinning the full vanilla list (rather than a project-scope subset) ensures any future runtime that accidentally probes for `doom2.wad` with the wrong order is detected by the audit. The reference handler intentionally collapses the search-directory parameter to a `void searchDirectory;` no-op when consulting `presentBasenames` because the virtual filesystem state only carries basenames; this means the audit witnesses the DOOMWADDIR-overrides-cwd invariant only at the candidate-list level, not at the resolved-full-path level. A future oracle-capture step that observes `doom/DOOMD.EXE` directly under controlled `DOOMWADDIR` settings (or instruments the `access()` calls in `linuxdoom-1.10`) would extend this audit to pin the full-path resolution. The audit module imports a `type` alias from `src/bootstrap/gameMode.ts` (the only runtime-source dependency) — a corruption of that file that broadened or narrowed the `GameMode` union would surface as a focused-test failure on the per-filename gameMode assertions because the candidate list is type-narrowed against the alias. The same recurring parallel-lane working-tree race documented in prior governance/inventory/oracle/wad/core lane HANDOFF_LOG entries is still active; on this step it surfaced as seven persistent failures in the untracked `src/core/audit-fixed-divide-semantics.ts` BigInt-reference function (real divide-by-zero bugs in another lane's mid-write file, not in this lane's write lock and never on main). The launch-lane focused test, the launch-lane test directory (143/143), the typecheck, and the plan-validation tests are all green; this commit only stages this lane's four files (the audit module, the focused test, MASTER_CHECKLIST.md, HANDOFF_LOG.md), leaving the parallel lanes' uncommitted files for those lanes to handle. ## 2026-04-26 - 04-003 audit-fixed-divide-semantics

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- lane: core
- lock_id: 8e8565ef-3f37-4d3c-a83f-b7599f0d1e20
- step_id: 04-003
- step_title: audit-fixed-divide-semantics
- summary: Pinned the vanilla DOOM 1.9 fixed-point divide semantics implemented by `fixedDiv` in `src/core/fixed.ts`. Wrote `src/core/audit-fixed-divide-semantics.ts` as a self-contained audit ledger that does not import from `src/core/fixed.ts` (so a corruption in fixed.ts cannot silently corrupt the probe table that detects the corruption). The audit module exports four hand-pinned canonical constants (`AUDITED_FRACBITS = 16`, `AUDITED_FRACUNIT = 65_536`, `AUDITED_FIXED_MAX = 0x7FFFFFFF`, `AUDITED_FIXED_MIN = -0x80000000`), a ten-entry `FIXED_DIV_AUDIT` ledger with stable identifier types covering five `c-source` facts (the `m_fixed.h` header signature `fixed_t FixedDiv(fixed_t a, fixed_t b);`, the canonical guard predicate `if ((abs(a) >> 14) >= abs(b))` from `m_fixed.c`, the sign-XOR clamp return `return (a^b) < 0 ? INT_MIN : INT_MAX;`, the canonical non-overflow body `result = ((int64_t) a << 16) / b;`, and the implicit narrowing cast `return (fixed_t) result;`), four `divide-rule` facts (`GUARD_CAPTURES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO` — divide-by-zero is captured by `abs(b) == 0` making `>= 0` trivially true; `GUARD_CLAMP_SIGN_FROM_XOR` — sign-XOR clamp follows the operand sign on b == 0; `NON_OVERFLOW_TRUNCATES_TOWARD_ZERO` — C99 integer division rounds toward zero, asymmetric with FixedMul's arithmetic-right-shift; `FIXED_MIN_NUMERATOR_BYPASSES_GUARD_VIA_X86_ABS_PARITY` — `abs(INT_MIN) == INT_MIN` on x86 wraps to negative, the guard misses, and `(int64) FIXED_MIN << 16 / b` wraps modulo 2^32, including the documented JS-vs-C divergence at `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 0) == 0` because JS float `(-Infinity | 0) == 0` while C integer divide-by-zero crashes), and one `js-implementation` fact pinning the `((a * 0x10000) / b) | 0` float-divide-then-narrow form in `src/core/fixed.ts` as bounded by 2^47 (well below `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER`) with float rounding error below 1 ulp at the int32 quotient magnitude. It exports a seven-entry `FIXED_DIV_INVARIANTS` ledger (GUARD_CATCHES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO_FOR_EVERY_NUMERATOR — with documented FIXED_MIN exclusion; GUARD_CLAMP_FOLLOWS_SIGN_XOR; IDENTITY_BY_FRACUNIT_DIVISOR; IDENTITY_BY_SELF_DIVISOR — with documented FIXED_MIN exclusion; ZERO_DIVIDEND_ABSORBS_FOR_NON_ZERO_DIVISOR — with documented FIXED_MIN-divisor exclusion; INT32_RANGE_RESULT; AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE), and a 25-entry curated `FIXED_DIV_PROBES` table covering nine categories (identity, zero-dividend, integer, fractional, truncation, divide-by-zero, overflow-guard, boundary, fixed-min-bypass) with hand-derived `expected` values for each. Each probe carries a `guardTriggers: boolean` flag pinning whether the canonical guard is expected to fire for the input pair, and the focused test cross-checks that flag against the canonical guard predicate computed independently. The hand-derived expectations include the canonical x86 abs-parity bypass cases (`fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 1) == 0` via int48 -2^47 wrap, `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, -1) == 0` via int48 +2^47 wrap, `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, FRACUNIT) == FIXED_MIN` via exact division, `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, FIXED_MIN) == FIXED_MAX` via guard-triggers-when-both-sides-negative path), the toward-zero truncation rule (`fixedDiv(-7, FRACUNIT*3) == -2` not -3, distinguishing FixedDiv from FixedMul's arithmetic-right-shift floor), the divide-by-zero clamp by sign (FRACUNIT/0 = FIXED_MAX, -FRACUNIT/0 = FIXED_MIN, 0/0 = FIXED_MAX), the just-at and just-below boundary at numerator = 16384*FRACUNIT (boundary triggers FIXED_MAX clamp because `>=` is exact-equality at 65536 = 65536, just-below preserves the input via the non-overflow branch). It exports a `fixedDivReference(a, b)` BigInt-based reference implementation that mirrors the canonical two-branch C body and explicitly handles `b == 0` on the non-overflow branch by returning 0 (matching the JS implementation's `-Infinity | 0` route, since the canonical C body would crash on integer divide-by-zero), and a `crossCheckFixedDivSemantics(fixedDivFn)` helper that returns failure ids `probe:<id>` for any per-probe expectation mismatch and `invariant:<id>` for any derived-invariant violation across the full probe-input sweep. The cross-check explicitly skips `valueInt32 === FIXED_MIN` for both the divide-by-zero and zero-dividend invariant sweeps to honour the documented FIXED_MIN bypass, and skips when the self-guard would trigger for `IDENTITY_BY_SELF_DIVISOR` (covering the FIXED_MIN/FIXED_MIN guard-fires case). Wrote the focused test `test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-fixed-divide-semantics.test.ts` (48 tests, 538 expects) that asserts the audited canonical constants agree with the runtime exports from `src/core/fixed.ts`, locks the ledger shape (exactly 10 facts split 5/4/1 across categories, 7 invariants, 25 probes covering 9 categories, every probe's guardTriggers flag agrees with the canonical guard predicate), pins specific fact values (the verbatim C signature/guard-predicate/clamp-return/body strings, the int32-only operand/expected typing for every probe), verifies the BigInt reference agrees with every probe expectation AND with an inline independent BigInt reference (mirroring the C body without sharing code) on a 15x15 sweep of representative int32 values (225 cross-checks, with `b == 0` handled by returning 0 in both references to match JS behaviour), runs `crossCheckFixedDivSemantics(fixedDiv)` against the live runtime and asserts zero failures, asserts the runtime honours every documented invariant on the canonical extremes (`fixedDiv(FRACUNIT, 0) === FIXED_MAX`, `fixedDiv(-FRACUNIT, 0) === FIXED_MIN`, `fixedDiv(0, 0) === FIXED_MAX`, the three FIXED_MIN bypass cases, the boundary at 16384*FRACUNIT triggers vs 16383*FRACUNIT preserves), and proves six distinct failure-mode tampering candidates are detected: (1) an off-by-one `>` instead of `>=` guard predicate fails `probe:overflow_at_boundary_16384_FRACUNIT` and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; (2) a no-sign-XOR always-FIXED_MAX clamp fails `probe:divide_by_zero_negative_returns_FIXED_MIN`, `probe:overflow_neg_FIXED_MAX_div_one`, `invariant:GUARD_CLAMP_FOLLOWS_SIGN_XOR`, and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; (3) a Math.floor-based candidate that floors instead of truncating toward zero fails `probe:truncation_neg_seven_div_three_FRACUNIT` and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; (4) a no-narrowing candidate that returns the raw float result fails `probe:wrap_FIXED_MIN_div_one_to_zero` and `invariant:INT32_RANGE_RESULT`; (5) a NaN-on-divide-by-zero candidate fails `probe:divide_by_zero_positive_returns_FIXED_MAX` and `invariant:GUARD_CATCHES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO_FOR_EVERY_NUMERATOR`; (6) a Math.abs-based candidate that collapses the FIXED_MIN bypass fails `probe:wrap_FIXED_MIN_div_one_to_zero`, `probe:wrap_FIXED_MIN_div_neg_one_to_zero`, and `invariant:AGREES_WITH_BIGINT_REFERENCE`; the BigInt reference itself reports zero failures. Three step-file tests lock the `## lane: core` declaration, the `## write lock` paths, the `## research sources` listing of `m_fixed.c` / `tables.c` / `d_main.c` / `g_game.c`, and the `## prerequisites: 00-018` declaration. Marked 04-003 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.
- files_changed: D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/src/core/audit-fixed-divide-semantics.ts; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/test/vanilla_parity/core/audit-fixed-divide-semantics.test.ts; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md; D:/Projects/doom-in-typescript/plan_vanilla_parity/HANDOFF_LOG.md
- recovery_edit: First focused-test pass after authoring the audit module flagged seven failures: three on the live runtime fixedDiv (`invariant:GUARD_CATCHES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO_FOR_EVERY_NUMERATOR`, `invariant:ZERO_DIVIDEND_ABSORBS_FOR_NON_ZERO_DIVISOR`, `invariant:IDENTITY_BY_SELF_DIVISOR`) and four BigInt RangeError crashes in tampered-candidate tests (the `>` tamper, the `always FIXED_MAX` tamper, the floor tamper, the no-narrow tamper) plus one in the BigInt reference. Diagnosed the root cause as the documented x86 `abs(INT_MIN)` parity hole interacting with the cross-check sweep: (a) `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 0)` returns 0 in JS (via `-Infinity | 0`), not a clamp, because `abs(FIXED_MIN) >> 14 == -131072` does not satisfy `>= 0`, so the guard misses; (b) `fixedDiv(0, FIXED_MIN)` returns FIXED_MIN, not 0, because `abs(FIXED_MIN)` wraps negative and `0 >= -2^31` is true, so the guard triggers; (c) `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, FIXED_MIN)` returns FIXED_MAX (per probe 24's own pinned expectation), not FRACUNIT, because the guard triggers; (d) tampered candidates that fall through to BigInt division crash on `b == 0` because BigInt rejects zero divisors. Fixed by: (1) updating `fixedDivReference` to handle `b == 0` on the non-overflow branch by returning 0 (matching the JS implementation's float-Infinity narrowing); (2) explicitly skipping `valueInt32 === FIXED_MIN` for the GUARD_CATCHES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO_FOR_EVERY_NUMERATOR sweep (with the FIXED_MIN bypass documented in the invariant description); (3) explicitly skipping `valueInt32 === FIXED_MIN` for the ZERO_DIVIDEND_ABSORBS_FOR_NON_ZERO_DIVISOR sweep (with the FIXED_MIN-divisor exclusion documented); (4) computing `selfGuardWouldTrigger` for IDENTITY_BY_SELF_DIVISOR and skipping when the self-guard would trigger (covering the FIXED_MIN/FIXED_MIN guard-fires case); (5) extending the FIXED_MIN_NUMERATOR_BYPASSES_GUARD_VIA_X86_ABS_PARITY fact description to cover the `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 0) == 0` JS-vs-C divergence; (6) rewriting all six tampered candidates to use the JS `((aInt32 * 0x10000) / bInt32) | 0` non-overflow body (which doesn't crash on `b == 0`, just narrows ±Infinity to 0) instead of BigInt division. After these fixes the focused test passes 48/48, the full suite passes 9122/9122, and the typecheck is clean.

- open_risks: The audit pins a documented JS-vs-C divergence at `fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 0)`: the JS implementation returns 0 (via `-Infinity | 0`), while the canonical C body crashes on integer divide-by-zero (undefined behaviour, raises a hardware fault on x86). The audit acknowledges this divergence in the FIXED_MIN_NUMERATOR_BYPASSES_GUARD_VIA_X86_ABS_PARITY fact description but does not require the JS implementation to crash on this input — vanilla DOOM 1.9 demos and gameplay never call `FixedDiv(INT_MIN, 0)` (the only call sites that could theoretically pass `INT_MIN` as numerator pre-check the divisor for non-zero), so the divergence is non-load-bearing. A future oracle-capture step that observes `doom/DOOMD.EXE` under DOSBox with a deliberately constructed `FixedDiv(INT_MIN, 0)` invocation would extend this audit to pin the crash behaviour, but the project's primary acceptance criterion is parity on real demos and gameplay, not on undefined-behaviour edge cases. The cross-check's `GUARD_CATCHES_DIVIDE_BY_ZERO_FOR_EVERY_NUMERATOR` and `ZERO_DIVIDEND_ABSORBS_FOR_NON_ZERO_DIVISOR` invariants explicitly skip FIXED_MIN to honour this divergence; the `IDENTITY_BY_SELF_DIVISOR` invariant skips when the self-guard would trigger (covering FIXED_MIN/FIXED_MIN). A future runtime change to `src/core/fixed.ts` that switched from float-divide to BigInt-divide would change the FIXED_MIN/0 behaviour from 0 to a thrown RangeError, surfacing as a runtime crash rather than a silent divergence — that change is not on the current plan. The same recurring parallel-lane working-tree race documented in prior governance/inventory/oracle/wad/launch lane HANDOFF_LOG entries is still active; for this commit the working tree is clean of parallel-lane WIP files (the launch lane's 03-004 commit already landed). Lane lock `8e8565ef-3f37-4d3c-a83f-b7599f0d1e20` is held by the launcher and will be released on normal exit. - summary: Added the current-state inventory artifact for the player source surface at `plan_vanilla_parity/current-state/inventory-player-modules.json`. The snapshot scopes `src/player/` as the audited directory, enumerates the eight committed modules sorted by path (hitscan.ts, movement.ts, pickups.ts, playerSpawn.ts, powerups.ts, projectiles.ts, weaponStates.ts, weapons.ts), and partitions them into six role groups (`player_attacks`, `player_movement`, `player_pickups`, `player_powerups`, `player_state`, `player_weapons`). Per-module fingerprints capture size_bytes, line_count, sha256, exported interfaces, functions, constants, classes, types, `export const enum` declarations, external imports, and per-module src/ and test/ importer counts, plus a Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 vanilla-concept anchor for each module (P_Punch/P_Saw/P_FirePistol psprite actions, P_Thrust/P_CalcHeight/P_MovePlayer ticcmd application, P_GiveBody/P_GiveArmor/P_GiveCard/P_GivePower/P_TouchSpecialThing pickup behavior, the d_player.h player_t struct with P_SetPsprite/P_BringUpWeapon/P_SetupPsprites and G_PlayerReborn helpers, the P_PlayerInSpecialSector powerup tic and ST_doPaletteStuff palette/colormap selection, P_SpawnPlayerMissile/P_CheckMissileSpawn/P_ExplodeMissile/A_BFGSpray projectile behavior, the A_WeaponReady/A_Lower/A_Raise/A_ReFire/A_CheckReload/A_GunFlash/A_Light0..2 weapon state machine plus P_FireWeapon/P_DropWeapon, and P_GiveAmmo/P_GiveWeapon/P_GiveBackpack/P_CheckAmmo ammo accounting). The artifact records the test root `test/player/` with the eight focused tests, the reference manifest alignment for `MAXPLAYERS`, the canonical `TICRATE = 35`, and the Chocolate Doom source files `p_map.c`, `p_mobj.c`, `p_pspr.c`, `p_user.c` cross-checked against `reference/manifests/source-catalog.json`, the source-only player boundary, implications for downstream player-lane work (Player record reuse footprint of 13 src/ and 14 test importers, injected attack callbacks via HitscanContext/ProjectileContext, DEH_-prefixed tunable defaults, world-side dependency on `src/world/zMovement.ts`, and the MAXPLAYERS=4 fixed-size constraint), and concrete follow-up step links across the Phase 07 player-and-weapon arc (07-001..07-006 movement and reborn, 07-010..07-017 pickups and weapon ownership, 07-025..07-028 attack and weapon state actions, 07-032/07-033 player and weapon parity gates). Added the focused test `test/vanilla_parity/current-state/inventory-player-modules.test.ts`, which re-derives the inventory from the local tree, verifies all module fingerprints and import/export metadata, confirms every listed module has test importer coverage, validates the partition into the six role groups, checks reference-manifest values and source-catalog alignment without embedding WAD bytes, checks the step write-lock declaration, and includes failure-mode tests for a misclassified attack module, a bogus sha256, a wrong MAXPLAYERS limit, and a dropped player test root. Marked 01-008 complete in `plan_vanilla_parity/MASTER_CHECKLIST.md`.
